Deng Mingjie Discusses the Situation of Bandit Suppression in Sichuan | Hopes the Central Government will Provide Funds |

Deng Mingjie, the representative of the Sichuan Pacification Commissioner stationed in Shanghai, went to Sichuan last month on official business. He passed through Hubei and Beijing and returned to Shanghai the night before last. Yesterday, the reporter interviewed Mr. Deng to inquire about the situation of bandit suppression in Sichuan. Mr. Deng said that around the 20th of last month, due to the ineffective operations of Yang Sen's troops, Yingqu and Liang counties were lost. Subsequently, Liu Cunhou's troops collapsed without a fight, and Suiding fell into the hands of the bandits. At that time, Sheng and Zhang indeed felt a momentary threat. Later, the 21st Army changed to the front line, and the situation changed. From then until now, after more than 20 battles of various sizes, the bandits gradually retreated, and casualties were also high. There are currently about 40,000 guns in the hands of the bandits in Sichuan, but this is not enough to be feared. Given time, they can certainly be eliminated. Commissioner Liu is now proceeding to gradually reduce the bandit area from the military aspect, seeking to completely resolve this group of bandits within the scope of the province and prevent them from disturbing neighboring provinces. However, he feels extremely difficult in raising military expenses and local post-war funds. It is well known that the burden on the people of Sichuan is heavy. At this time, if we seek other income in the province, it is bound to increase the burden on the people, and the people are really unable to bear it after this disaster. What's more, the bandits are using heresies to bewilder the people, and it is absolutely inappropriate to give them more excuses. Therefore, regarding this expense, we still cannot help but hope that the central government will find a way to provide sufficient relief. The bandit suppression in Sichuan is different from the situation in Jiangxi. In Jiangxi, most of the troops are transferred from other provinces, while in Sichuan, they are purely local troops. Sichuan has many mountainous areas, and the troops are well-trained in mountain climbing. The bandit cadres come from other provinces and lack this ability, so the bandits in Jiangxi can only rely on the mountains, while the bandits in Sichuan are at a disadvantage in the mountains. Furthermore, the peasants in Sichuan are not easily threatened by bandit propaganda due to various reasons. This is another weakness of the bandits in Sichuan. Mr. Deng also showed a telegram from Liu Xiang to Chuan Zhenwu and Deng, saying that someone named Qian is falsely using the name of my representative to swagger around Hong Kong and Guangdong. After investigation, there is no such person as Qian among the representatives of our army. He hopes to make a statement to all parties to avoid confusing the audience. (Guowen News Agency)

A Sightseeing Record of Xiangfan by Ren An, a Special Correspondent of the Newspaper from Jiangxi, Anhui, Hunan, and Hubei

Xiangfan Correspondence: From Zaoyang to Xiangfan, the car galloped along a 200-li journey, mostly on winding mountain roads, with few people. Occasionally, two or three villages could be found, with clustered houses, each numbering over a hundred, surrounded by deep earth walls and trenches, resembling small towns. Otherwise, it would be impossible to live there for a day. It is said that this area has suffered from repeated disasters of bandits and drought, and recently even bloodshed. Although small villages have been merged into large villages to avoid remote mountains and live in the plains, the population is still small, the livelihood is difficult, and the social atmosphere is particularly bleak. The car was carrying goods, and there was only enough space for four passengers. Among them was a sickly-looking person, thin and pale, wearing ragged clothes, who looked to be only fourteen or fifteen years old. He was riding for free. When asked about his background, he said, "My name is Xiao Shitou, my surname is Wang, and I am from the Shihuyao in Xiangyang. In June of the lunar calendar, there was a garrison withdrawing to Hankou, and they sealed my family's blue mule, worth 42 yuan, saying that they would pay for grass and feed every day. My mother was reluctant to let it go, so she ordered me to follow them. When we arrived in Hankou, the brigade took a boat to Nanchang. Because I had no money to go home, I stayed in Hankou for two months. I couldn't communicate with my family. When I recovered a little, I began to beg my way back. Tonight, I will be able to see my mother." As he spoke, tears streamed down his face. The reporter happened to have a few loose coins and politely offered them to him. He initially refused firmly, but later only kept one coin to pay for the ferry across the Han River. The car crossed the Tangbai River, passed Zhangjiawan, where ships and warehouses were piled high with cotton, like a cotton collection place. Another 15 li brought us to Fancheng. It was still early, so we crossed the Han River and stayed overnight in Xiangyang.

The so-called Xiangfan refers to Xiangyang and Fancheng. The Han River flows south from here and suddenly bends eastward, meeting the Tangbai River, and then flows south again. The current gradually becomes turbulent, but in this bay, it is very slow. The river surface is even wider than the entrance to the Yangtze River in Hankou by more than twice. Anchoring here can avoid the north wind. The two cities sit facing each other across the Han River's bend, with Fancheng on this side and Xiangyang to the south, about a li apart. The ferry takes 20 minutes. They form a strategic stronghold. The Xianghua, Xiangsha, and Xiangyun motor roads intersect here. In ancient times, it was a strategic place for military campaigns in the north and south. Today, it still retains its important geographical significance. Xiangcheng is named after the Xiang Canal in the southwest. The canal is Tanxi, where it is popularly believed that Mr. Liu jumped across on his horse. The Han River from Xiangyang to Hankou is also called the Xiang River. It is a common mistake that Xiangyang is named after the river, but this is not the case.

The streets of Xiangfan are paved with stone, and are relatively wide and tidy, but not clean. Mud and tiles obstruct the way, and piles of feces, grass, and urine are everywhere, emitting a foul odor. The houses are very short, built in the northern style to prevent wind and snow in winter. They are all fitted with ceilings, and each courtyard has a pit for water drainage. Rainwater accumulates and has no way to drain out, only waiting for natural evaporation and underground absorption. In addition, the fuel used is mostly wheat straw, sesame stalks, sorghum stalks, cotton stalks, and other things. The food is especially fond of deep-fried dough cakes and the like. The smoke and oily smell is unbearable everywhere. With the air so unclean, it is no wonder that many people in the city suffer from eye diseases, with red and rotten eyelids, groping their way along. In the countryside, there are also many people with scabby heads. Old men are bald, and children's heads are covered with scabs, accounting for five or six out of ten. These two diseases are very contagious, especially in the countryside, where people like to use other people's towels and clothing, which is especially harmful. If local people do not actively promote hygiene and passively improve bad habits, what can be said about the impact on the future of health in the entire area? In other places, such as the so-called Shijingchong area, where nine out of ten farmers suffer from abdominal distention, gradually becoming emaciated to the point of death, the number of widows is no less than in the extremely tropical southern India. People attribute it to poor water and soil, and the hard work of the men in the fields. This may or may not be true, but the failure to pay attention to hygiene and prevent infectious diseases is undoubtedly the main reason.

Xiangfan is connected to Henan and Shaanxi in the north, and the livestock industry is quite prosperous. Before the Ping-Han Railway was opened, leather from the south mostly converged here. Although it is no longer what it used to be, there are still many residents engaged in making leather goods. However, due to the long-term blockade of the Han River by bandits, products such as leather trunks, sesame, sesame oil, glutinous rice, and Xiang sugar (that is, glutinous rice candy, whose name is similar to Xiaogan sesame candy) used to sell well in Wuhan, but are now gradually declining. Cotton is still mostly collected and loaded here, and transported in large quantities to the south. However, the clothing and cloth worn in this area are all shipped from Wuhan. The price of cotton is low (only 20 to 30 cents per foot), and the price of cloth is high. In addition, industrial consumables are small in quantity and expensive in quality. Cheaper car transport is the reason why it can fully enter the villages and towns and is a major economic leak for the people of this county. Recently, there has been a proposal to set up a cotton yarn textile factory locally, which is very pertinent. If it can become a reality, it will not only make business flourish.

Nitrate is the most abundant mineral, and rabbits are famous for being produced here. Nitrate can be found everywhere in the sandbars of Xiangcheng, just by looking down. As for the rabbit, a friend told the reporter when he was about to come here from Wuhan to be wary of rabbit bites. At the time, I thought it was a joke, or a coded phrase for bandit robbery, and I didn't believe it at all. Now, seeing that the villagers mostly sell rabbit meat, buying a head for only half a dime, I suddenly remembered my friend's advice and asked the tea servant. According to his reply, "It is not a false rumor that rabbits bite people." I was shocked to hear this. When I asked for the reason again, he continued, "For years, there have been severe droughts in Shaanxi and Henan, and the rabbits have no food to find, so they have gone south in groups, numbering thousands. Northern Xiangyang bears the brunt of this, and in that area, within hundreds of miles, bandits run rampant, and there are no people. The huts are deserted, and reeds grow everywhere, all becoming rabbit dens. They breed and multiply, much more than usual. In the morning and evening, solitary travelers are rarely disturbed. Even shepherds only ten li from the city have been harmed. Now, children in the northern countryside are scared to hear the frightening saying, 'The rabbits are coming to drag people away,' clutching their heads and running away in panic, even crying out loud, because the lessons of the past are enough to serve as a warning." I asked others again, and the answer was the same. This is not only a strange thing, but also a tragedy.

In terms of education, there is only one northern Hubei library for social education, located exclusively in Xiangcheng. It was founded by the former Northwest Army when they were stationed in Xiangyang. There are books and newspapers, and the management is good and the order is excellent. As for school education, there are provincial No. 3 Normal School, No. 5 Middle School, No. 12 Elementary School, and commercially run elementary schools. Among them, the No. 12 Elementary School has the best results. The rest need to be reorganized due to insufficient funding and lack of teachers. The political organs are the Commissioner's Office and the Xiang County Government. The administrative characteristic is in the prohibition of opium, but the exercise of power is always in conflict with the Hubei Special Tax Anti-Smuggling Office (each with a branch in Xiangfan at the ferry, facing each other across the river). Commissioner Liu Ji has achieved remarkable results in the orphanage and nursing home affairs of the Commissioner and is well-known to the people.

Famous scenic spots include Longzhong, the Dropped Tears Monument, the Wenxuan Terrace, the Haoran Pavilion, the Sheep-Du Temple, and Zhenwu Mountain. Among them, Longzhong is the most famous. In the 21st year of the Republic, Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek came to Xiangyang and visited the area. Seeing that the buildings had not been repaired for many years and the scenic spots were dilapidated, he couldn't bear to hear of them being submerged again. Therefore, he allocated funds for repairs and built a motor road to connect it. It is thirty li from the city. I once visited it with friends. The highway is only for special vehicles, and tourists still have to walk or hire a donkey to travel. Leaving the west gate of the city, passing under Zhenwu Mountain, reaching a high slope, seeing an ancient stele "Grave of the Wronged People Zhang Xingfa" and the "Rest Pavilion" repaired this time, with the Qunshan mountains standing in front, the shape of the pyramid-like Longzhong is now clearly in sight. Fifteen or sixteen li from here, the mountain slopes undulate like waves, the road is rugged, and there is no forest scenery, which greatly reduces the tourist interest. A friend joked, "The road to Longzhong is so difficult to walk, no wonder when Han Zhaolie (Liu Bei) visited Kongming (Zhuge Liang) three times, Zhang Fei couldn't bear the hard work and asked to drag him with a rope made of grass." Before long, we suddenly entered a dense and beautiful forest, treading on fragrant grass, searching for secluded paths. Thus, the Three Visit Hall, the Thatched Cottage Stele, the Ancient Cypress Pavilion, the Farming Field, the Liangfu Rock, the Hugging Knee Stone, the Old Dragon Cave, the Small Rainbow Bridge, the Yeyun Hut, the Half-Moon Creek, and other ten scenes were all viewed in order in the green bamboo and verdant pines, and a kind of noble and quiet air dispelled the worries of the world. Other things, such as the Zhongzheng Hall's incremental construction and the many clean and elegant inscriptions in the Wuhou Temple, are interspersed with the words "Responding as Resonantly" and the use of Taoist priests with queues to serve incense and candles. The meaning of this is probably nothing more than the appreciation of both the refined and the vulgar.

Prosper Qingdao Plan: Preliminary Plan of Qingdao Prosperity Promotion Association: Improving Internal Affairs and Attracting Tourists from Other Places

Qingdao Correspondence: The Qingdao Prosperity Promotion Association, since its establishment, has been actively researching and exploring strategies to promote the prosperity of Qingdao, hoping to make contributions. The association has now formulated the first step of the Qingdao City Prosperity Plan, which aims to awaken all sectors of the city, improve all internal affairs and construction, and vigorously promote the city to make domestic and foreign people understand all the advantages of Qingdao, so as to attract tourists from other places. The outline of the plan is excerpted as follows: (1) Attracting tourists from other places is the main goal of the prosperity plan. As for attracting tourists, it is nothing more than introducing the beauty and goodness of the city to major ports at home and abroad. The proposed publicity methods include: A. Printing artistic stationery and envelopes with colorful and exquisite depictions of the city's beautiful scenery, various constructions, and various aspects of living and entertainment, to promote the image of Qingdao through correspondence, so that people in other places will not forget Qingdao. B. Publishing more articles or pictures about Qingdao in famous magazines in major ports. C. Compiling and printing Chinese and Western pocket manuals with detailed information on Qingdao sightseeing itineraries, round-trip costs, and land and water transportation facilities, and distributing them in major cities to arouse the interest of the general public in visiting Qingdao. D. When necessary, selectively place timely advertisements in major Chinese and Western newspapers (such as the spring flower viewing festival and the summer sea bathing season) to attract public attention to Qingdao. E. Publishing Qingdao Fine Arts Special Editions. F. Using radio broadcasting to invite celebrities to give speeches on all issues related to Qingdao. G. Installing outdoor billboards in major ports with illustrations of Qingdao and Laoshan scenic spots and special products. H. Inviting famous writers to use the environment of Qingdao to create novel film scripts and inviting well-known film companies to come to Qingdao to produce films and screen them in other places for effective publicity. I. Publishing regular publications for year-round promotion.

(2) Improving internal affairs: A. Constructing medium-sized housing to meet the needs of the middle class. B. Constructing new-style hotels to accommodate summer tourists. C. Constructing public bathhouses, following the example of Guangzhou in the 16th year of the Republic of China, with the government providing capital and attracting merchants to contract. D. Inviting the financial community to establish silver companies to specialize in small, low-interest loans without requiring collateral, using store guarantees instead of pledges. E. Improving transportation. F. Improving the city appearance to make it artistic. G. Opening up new scenic areas and tidying them up. H. Expanding places for sightseeing and observation. I. Organizing municipal visiting groups to investigate and visit major cities. J. Separately soliciting books, charts, or models and specimens on municipal, industrial, commercial, and all prosperous undertakings from advanced cities at home and abroad, collecting them as much as possible, and then holding exhibitions to learn from them. (November 24)

Various Counties in Southern Anhui Province: Telephoning Requests to Exempt Salt Tax Increase: Taxing 17 or 18 Yuan per Load: Now Taxing an Additional One Yuan per Load

Huizhou Correspondence: The salt quotas of the counties in Huizhou Prefecture in southern Anhui Province have always belonged to Zhejiang Province, while the salt quotas of Wangjiang, Susong, Taihu, Qiupu, Zhide, and other counties in central Anhui Province have always belonged to Huaibei Province. In recent years, due to the increase in tax rates, the food households have already suffered from increased burdens. In remote counties such as Jixi County, salt costs seventeen or eighteen yuan per hundred catties, which is one-third higher than ten years ago. Recently, the salt in the counties of Huizhou Prefecture and central Anhui Province was ordered to increase by one yuan in tax per load. The food households in Huizhou Prefecture are suffering from years of disasters, famines, and banditry, and the people are in extreme hardship. Now, the sudden increase in such taxes makes it difficult for transporters and the public to obtain food. They have telegraphed overseas hometown associations to send separate telegrams to the Ministry of Finance, the Salt Affairs Administration, and the Zhejiang Salt Transport Envoy, requesting consideration of the people's difficulties and granting exemptions. They have also sent letters to public organizations in various counties to strive together to achieve results. The Chambers of Commerce of Zhide and other counties in central Anhui Province have also telegraphed the provincial government, earnestly requesting that the Ministry of Finance and the General Inspectorate of Salt Affairs be forwarded to withdraw the established case of adding one yuan of salt tax to Wangjiang, Susong, Taihu, and other counties to alleviate the people's difficulties. It is reported that the provincial government, after receiving the telegram, has consulted the Ministry of Finance to investigate whether the order to increase the salt tax by one yuan in Wangjiang, Susong, and Taihu counties by the Datong Salt Affairs Weighing and Release Office was issued with permission from the Ministry and whether it was notified in advance to avoid doubts and requested verification and reply.

Anhui Province: Jianghuai Main Embankment Project: Economic Commission Replies That No Funds Can Be Allocated: Construction Department Instructs Counties to Collect Labor for Handling

Anqing Correspondence: The Jianghuai main embankments within Anhui Province were repaired with government relief after the flood in the twentieth year of the Republic of China but could not be fully completed. In August of last year, they were transferred to the Engineering Office of the National Economic Commission for handling. Due to tight funding, not much supplementation was added. During the major flood this year, there were many dangerous spots. The Construction Department sent personnel to protect them in sections, and no major disaster occurred. However, there were many places where the embankments needed to be heightened and thickened, or the embankment line retreated and extension dams added. Moreover, after being washed away by the flood, many sections were eroded and collapsed. The situation was the same on the Huai embankment. The Construction Department repeatedly received requests from the people and forwarded them to the National Economic Commission, urging them to handle it quickly. Recently, the commission replied that the funds allocated to the Engineering Office of the commission to take over the unfinished projects of the Flood Relief Committee have already been fully distributed. There are no more funds to allocate for the embankment projects that should be repaired in the Jianghuai region of Anhui Province. They should be handled on their own. The department has already ordered the counties along the Jiang and Huai rivers to handle it themselves as soon as possible. However, since this is a major project, it may be difficult to achieve the desired results by relying solely on the counties. Therefore, it replied to the Economic Commission to negotiate and requested that a bureau be established to carry out the construction and requested the provincial government to send a telegram to urge it. At the same time, it quickly sought its own solutions to avoid delays. It plans to assign the project to the counties for labor collection and have the province send personnel to supervise and guide them in sections. If the Economic Commission establishes a bureau for construction, these personnel stationed in sections can assist. If they do not come to handle it or only agree to provide some funding for labor, these personnel are even more indispensable. Therefore, it has drafted measures for supervising the repair of the Jianghuai main embankments based on the actual situation, dividing the Jiang embankment into twelve sections and the Huai embankment into six sections, totaling eighteen sections. There will be one general inspector for the Jiang and Huai rivers and twenty supervisors. The work will last for six months from December 1 of this year to the end of May next year. Except for the general inspector, who will be rotated by the department without additional expenses, the total cost of supervision will be 12,880 yuan, which will be forwarded to the provincial government for approval to be paid from the remaining funds of 50,000 yuan from the original flood prevention funds for this year, with the Finance Department allocating it monthly. (November 24)

Jiangsu Province: Water Police Reorganization Completed: Six Districts Changed to Four Districts

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The Jiangsu Provincial Government has decided to reorganize the water police in the entire province, reducing the original six districts to four. It ordered each district to uniformly reorganize all its teams. According to the district chiefs of the fifth and sixth districts, Gong Guoliang, regarding the reorganization of the water police, the following is recorded:

Gong said that Jiangsu Province originally had six water police districts, governing twenty-five teams. The first, second, and third districts each governed five major teams, the fourth district governed three teams, the fifth district governed four teams, and the sixth district governed three teams. There was also a guerrilla team directly under the department, stationed around Suzhou, and a special service team under the jurisdiction of the fourth district, stationed around Nantong. Now, the four major districts have been merged, with the first and second districts merged into the first district, stationed in Minhang, the third district changed to the second district, stationed in Suzhou, the fourth district changed to the third district, stationed in Nantong, and the fifth and sixth districts merged into the fourth district, stationed in Guazhou. The teams under the jurisdiction of each district include four major teams in the first district, six major teams in the second district, four major teams in the third district, and five major teams in the fourth district. The guerrilla team and the special service team have been canceled. All soldiers and guerrillas have been merged into the second district, and the special service team has been merged into the third district. The reorganization of the major teams in each district has been completed. ▲ The chiefs of the four districts have been appointed. After receiving the order to reorganize, Gong ordered all subordinate teams to rush to complete all procedures by the 28th. After the reorganization, the organization and consolidation work continued. The leaders of the four districts have been appointed, with the leader of the fifteenth team concurrently held by Gong himself in accordance with the department's order, the leader of the sixteenth team being Shen Hualong, the leader of the seventeenth team being Wu Zhishan, the leader of the eighteenth team being Zhang Liyou, and the leader of the nineteenth team being Li Panming. The budget for this reorganization was originally more than 104,000 yuan, but the provincial treasury was insufficient, and only enough was issued to pay the remaining salaries for June, July, August, and September to those who left their posts, as well as the salaries for October and November. The salaries of those who were taking their place have not been paid. (28th)

Yu Surname Family in Songjiang East Outer Suburb Startled After Robbery

Yu Henian's family in Dongwai is quite famous for its wealth. At the end of this month, bandits robbed them of more than 400 yuan in cash and jewelry, but the case has not yet been solved. Since the original police force in Dongwai was insufficient, a squad from the county police team was dispatched to station there. On this day (28th) at around 1:00 PM, three people wearing Western suits and Zhongshan suits with accents entered and closed the gate, barging straight into the accounting room and forcibly borrowing travel expenses, making a lot of noise. The family members, knowing that something was wrong, immediately telegraphed the Fourth Precinct Station to send the police, who detained the three people. Upon questioning, they identified themselves as Liu Guoping, Li Guokai, and Yang Jun, all from Hunan. Nineteenth Route Army badges were found on them. They claimed to be veterans of the Nineteenth Route Army passing through and borrowing money for travel expenses without any other intention. They tore up the documents on their persons and threw them into the toilet. Outside the gate, two Jiangbei people, Hu Weiming and Chen Dehan, who were selling herbs, were also arrested and taken to the bureau for interrogation.

In the case of the murder of Xi Weisheng and his wife at Huayang Bridge, Shen Ahe, who was caught holding a gun, and Wu Zixiang and Xi Weiquan, who were suspected, were prosecuted. During the two court sessions, they both recanted their previous confessions. Yesterday, Judge Zhang Yi Huang personally inspected the situation of Maozhu Port and the mud embankment behind the Xi family's house at Huayang Bridge. This morning, another court session was held. Expansion of Suzhou Vegetable Market Dispute

The dispute in the vegetable market west of the city, where the Public Security Bureau forced vegetable vendors, triggering a brief strike by shops inside Xumen, was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday (28th) at 5:00 AM, Inspector Li Yin of the Fifth Precinct and Inspectors Tang Liu and Li of nearby precincts led long police squads. The Second Bureau dispatched a flying team, and the Public Security Bureau dispatched three inspectors to guard all entrances in the Daoqian Street and Yuyuxiang areas, prohibiting vegetable vendors from carrying vegetables into the alley and ordering them to carry them to the Xilikucai vegetable market for business. At that time, chefs from Wang Yiji Sauce Garden in Yuyuxiang and Daji Cloth Shop and other places purchased large quantities of vegetables, fish, and meat from other places for meals, but they were also prevented from entering the alley. In addition, Xie Fuyuan Cake Shop also sold salted fish due to sluggish business, which was also interfered with. Representatives from various shops, including Ye Yinping (Wang Yiji), Wang Jiasheng (Daji), Zhang Linsheng (Xie Fuyuan), and Feng Xunfu (Lao Wannian Silver Shop), and nine others went to the Public Security Bureau to petition, but the result was unsatisfactory. They then went to the county government with the aim of requesting freedom of business and convenient transportation. By that time, it was 10:00 AM. Meanwhile, the vegetable vendors, after this disturbance, had not sold the vegetables they had carried. They gathered forty or fifty people and went to the county government, claiming to sell to the county magistrate, and throwing radishes and other things into the gate of the county government, resulting in a conflict with the police guarding the gate. Four vegetable vendors, including Zhang Ada (female, only fourteen years old, living at No. 3 Cailian Alley nearby) and Wu Baofu, were injured by the police. Later, Secretary Wang of the county government persuaded the representatives of the shops and sent them away, and Zhang Ada and others were sent to Guangmin Hospital for treatment. At 1:00 PM, shops in Daoqian Street, Yuyuxiang, and other places gathered to discuss organizing a joint association and appointed representatives to continue to request attention from the Chamber of Commerce and the County Party Department at around 2:00 PM. If there was no result by night, they prepared to submit a report to the provincial government and call for help.

Female Worker at Wuxi Yarn Factory Dies Tragically

Wu Asi, a female child worker, aged sixteen, from Yancheng, at the Zhenxin Yarn Factory outside Ximen, was transferring yarn from the fine yarn section to the cloth machine section upstairs at around 4:00 PM the day before yesterday. Asi took the elevator up, but Asi, being young and playful, stuck her head out of the elevator. Unexpectedly, in a split second, the elevator had risen close to the floor, but Asi did not notice and continued to stick her head out, causing her head to be crushed between the floor and the elevator. Brain matter splattered instantly, and she died immediately. The corpse fell from above, covered in blood and flesh, a tragic sight. Later, the factory notified her mother, Wu Zhang, who came to the factory and mourned loudly. Yesterday morning (28th), Pan Yunzhang, the head of the factory, reported the incident to the County Court. Prosecutor Shen led officials to conduct an autopsy and confirmed that she died from being crushed. After the autopsy, the factory prepared a coffin for burial.

Party and Government Agencies Strictly Prohibit Petitioning

The County Party Department and the County Government of this county, in view of the recent disputes among silk factory workers and garment industry workers over salary issues or business competition, often resulting in gatherings and processions for petitions, although they have been dealt with impartially and can be resolved gradually, believe that this situation of public disorder is not only unsightly but also easily affects public security. Therefore, it should be strictly prohibited. Yesterday, a joint announcement was issued to all industries and people in the county, informing them that if any difficulties arise in various industries in the future, they may submit a written request or send representatives to state their case, and there will be proper channels for resolution. Those who dare to violate this will be dealt with severely.

Du Xigui Leads Students to Nanjing on the Same Ship Last Night; The Sanbei Wanxiang Ship Will Pass Through the Capital Tomorrow; The Ships Stationed in Shanghai Will Sail to Sanduao to Assemble

Another Civil War Breaks Out in Guizhou; Shanghai Students Interrogate Qiu Yunchang, but Qiu Denies Representing Mao Guangxiang

In Guizhou Province, the war between Mao Guangxiang and Wang Jialie has been going on for years, and the people have been suffering greatly. Last year, You Guocai, Jiang Jiazhen, and others fought fiercely with Wang Jialie several times, and were finally defeated by Wang and retreated to the border of Sichuan and Yunnan. After Wang designated eight counties in Panjiang as You's defense area, You also expressed his willingness to lead his troops to leave Guizhou and participate in the war against Japan, seemingly maintaining temporary peace. Now, the changes in Jiang's troops in Xiamen have also failed. Recently, a mixed war between the Mao and Wang factions has broken out again within Guizhou Province. Mao Guangxiang has also sent his confidant Qiu Yunchang (Wenbo) to Shanghai with a large sum of money to seek to regain control of Guizhou Province. The Guizhou students in this city are heartbroken by the tragedy of their hometown being ravaged by civil war for years, and on the morning of the day before yesterday, they went to Qiu Yunchang's residence on Bai'erbu Road to interrogate Qiu, expressing their opposition. Qiu said that the news of him carrying a large sum of money to Shanghai was fabricated by others, and that he was not entrusted by Mao. The civil war of the Guizhou warlords has nothing to do with him. He can publish an announcement in the newspaper the next day to clarify. The interrogators at that time said that the news of Qiu's activities in Shanghai had been published in newspapers for more than ten days, and it was not credible to make a clarification at this time. Moreover, the recent war in Guizhou has become more and more fierce, and the extreme opposition between Wang and Mao, and Mao's actions to overthrow Wang, have been detailed in newspapers, which is known to everyone. Anyone who participates in or plots the civil war of the Guizhou warlords should be responsible for the innocent people in Guizhou who have been ravaged. The two sides argued for several hours before leaving. The Guizhou youth in Shanghai also plan to issue a declaration opposing the ongoing and expanding civil war in Guizhou.

Preparing to Open a Special Express Ship Between Beijing and Hankou; 32 Hours Upstream, Only 24 Hours Downstream

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company plans to open a special express ship on the Yangtze River line between Beijing and Hankou, connecting with various railways. This matter was started before the E Ship ran aground. Recently, the Hubei Construction Department's Navigation Administration Office believes that the special express ship between Beijing and Hankou urgently needs to be opened, and has specially formulated measures to contact the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, stipulating that three ships should be dispatched. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has accepted its plan, and the shipping department has begun to plan and handle it. Details are checked and recorded as follows.

Reasons for Increasing Flights: Zhang Yanxiang, Director of the Navigation Administration Office of the Hubei Construction Department, proposed the Beijing-Hankou Express Ship because the Railway Department has now signed a water-land joint transportation contract with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. The amount of goods transported by the Yangtze River ship upstream and downstream will be more than other companies' ships. Cargo transportation and loading and unloading take time. Passengers traveling to and from various ports on the Yangtze River will definitely be taken away by foreign merchant ships on the same route. The transfer of profits is closely related to the business of domestic passenger transport, so it is necessary to increase the number of special express ships to save it.

Shortening the Journey: The current Yangtze River ship of Six Companies, if Nanjing is the starting point, the fastest time to reach Hankou upstream must be 52 hours. As for sailing downstream from Hankou, due to the favorable current, it is faster, but on average, each Yangtze River ship must also take 36 hours in the downstream flight. If the Beijing-Hankou Express Ship is changed, the unimportant docks will not be stopped, and the three ports of Beijing, Xun, and Han will be designated as official berthing ports. Then the upstream ship only needs 32 hours to reach the distance, and the downstream is faster, only 24 hours to reach the port. Each trip can shorten the journey by more than 30 hours.

Connecting Trains and Ships: The Beijing-Hankou Express Ship departs from Nanjing and is scheduled to connect to the Jinpu and Jinghu express trains at 10 a.m. It can also connect to the Nanxun Road express train at Jiujiang in the afternoon. The next day, it arrives in Hankou and can connect to the Wuchang express train. After staying in Hankou for one night, it departs at 9 a.m. the next morning and can connect to the Pinghan and Xiang'e express trains. The Xiang'e Pinghan and other roads have already been connected. Once the flights are opened, passengers will definitely be crowded.

Three Ships Specified: The Hubei Construction Department and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company consulted and requested that three Yangtze River ships be dispatched to meet the demand. Each ship travels once, and it takes about four days including berthing time. Compared with the current Yangtze River ship, which takes eight to nine days for each trip, the water income can naturally increase. With three ships, it is expected that one ship can be opened every day, and both Beijing and Hankou will have special express ships going back and forth every day.

Fares Determined: The Navigation Administration Office of the Hubei Construction Department also plans to divide the passenger fares for the upstream and downstream special express ships into three classes: first class, 24 yuan for upper deck cabin, 20 yuan for lower deck cabin, 36 yuan for upper deck berth, 30 yuan for lower deck berth; second class, 14 yuan for upper deck cabin, 24 yuan for berth, 12 yuan for lower deck cabin, 20 yuan for berth; third class, 8 yuan for upper deck cabin, 12 yuan for berth, 7 yuan for lower deck cabin, 10 yuan for berth.

The Jie Sheng Ship Returned to Shanghai from Fujian Yesterday

After the Fujian incident, Chinese merchant ships in Shanghai, such as Huaan, Taishun, and Wanxiang, have stopped sailing one after another. Currently, only the British Jardine Matheson's Jie Sheng ship and the Japanese Osaka Company's Changsha Maru, Fujian Maru, and Shengjing Maru are sailing between Shanghai and Fuzhou. As for the Nisshin Company's Nanhua ship, it only goes to Hong Kong and Guangdong and does not sail to Fujian, Xiamen, or Shantou. The Jie Sheng ship arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong yesterday afternoon. According to passengers on the ship, the Fujian authorities have started sealing and detaining merchant ships in Fujian ports since the 26th for military use. All Chinese merchant ships docked in Fuzhou that can be used at sea have been detained and are not allowed to leave the port. Fortunately, the Sanbei Wanxiang ship left Fujian on Saturday and sailed out a day earlier, so it was not sealed and detained. However, foreign merchant ships entering and leaving are not detained due to diplomatic relations, so they can still sail as usual. As for the Chinese merchant ships in Fujian, they all have to change to new flags. Yesterday, the Jie Sheng ship came to Shanghai. According to the crew, there was no sealing of ports in Fujian and Hong Kong.

The Fujian Salt Affairs Branch Office Operates as Usual; Manager Lu Wenlan Is Replaced by Deng Ruiren; Overdue Foreign Debts Are Still Returned on Time

After the political changes in Fujian Province, most of the central government's tax collection agencies in Fujian have been confiscated by the Fujian People's Government one after another. The Far East News Agency reporter asked whether the salt affairs tax revenue was also affected. Yesterday, he specially visited Zhu Tingqi, Director of the Salt Affairs Audit Office, and Fei Gongyan, the secretary sent to the office, met in his place.

Only the Manager Changed: Fei answered the reporter's question, first saying that after the Fujian Provincial Political Changes became a reality, this office was deeply afraid of suffering misfortune. However, things were unexpected. Except for Lu Wenlan, the Fuzhou Branch Manager and Manager, who was replaced by Deng Ruiren, the rest of the internal personnel did not move. The office is still operating as usual under the supervision of Ruiston, the British Assistant Manager.

Foreign Debt Is Still Remitted: He continued that the income of the Fuzhou Branch Office, in addition to the foreign debt, can be allocated on time. There has never been any surplus remittance to the head office, because the monthly income of the branch office is only more than 400,000 yuan, while the expenditure requires more than 500,000 yuan. The income is not enough to cover the expenditure, so there is no surplus to remit. Now the Fujian side has agreed to return the overdue foreign debt to the branch office on time, so the salt affairs tax revenue has not been affected in reality after the Fujian changes.

Lu Has Gone to Hong Kong: He also said that Lu Wenlan, the Fujian Salt Transport Envoy and Manager of the Fuzhou Branch Office of this office, reported that he had arrived in Shanghai from Fujian, which is not true. Lu originally planned to come to Shanghai directly from Fujian, but because he could not wait for a ship, he first took a boat to Hong Kong a few days ago. This office once sent a telegram to inquire about his whereabouts. According to the reply, he will take a boat to Shanghai from Hong Kong in the next few days and report everything to the Ministry of Finance in Beijing.

China Aviation Company's Shanghai-Guangdong Line's Aircraft No. 17 Departed on Time Yesterday; The Mail Left Over from the Previous Flight Was All Taken by the Aircraft; A Telegram Said That It Had Safely Arrived in Guangzhou at 5:50 p.m.

Since the official opening of the China Aviation Company's Shanghai-Guangdong route, it carried mail for one month and began to carry passengers on the 24th of this month. Unexpectedly, due to bad weather and dense fog, Aircraft No. 16 crashed into a mountain and fell into the sea near Zhoushan Island in Hangzhou Bay, resulting in injuries to all nine passengers and pilots. Aircraft No. 16 was also completely destroyed and could not be salvaged. Yesterday was the scheduled flight for the company's Shanghai-Guangdong route southbound. The reporter of the Dagong News Agency inquired about the flight situation. Mr. Liang Jingzhao of the company's business group told the following:

Departing on Time

According to Mr. Liang, Aircraft No. 17 was piloted by chief pilot Ge Situo and co-pilot Wu Te. It still took off from Longhua Airport on time at 6 a.m. this morning (i.e., yesterday morning). All the mail left over from the previous flight was taken by the aircraft. The scattered Guangdong mail was all completely recovered and also taken by the aircraft.

Number of Passengers

There were a total of seven passengers, five of whom got off in Fuzhou, and the other two went all the way to Guangzhou. However, when Aircraft No. 17 arrived in Fuzhou, there were five more passengers on board, two of whom went to Xiamen, two to Shantou, and the remaining one all the way to Guangzhou.

Arrived Safely in Guangdong

After Aircraft No. 17 departed from Shanghai, the company received a radio telegram from the aircraft, saying that it arrived in Shantou at 2:25 p.m. It departed from Shantou at 2:55 p.m. At 5:50 p.m., it received another telegram, saying that it had safely arrived in Guangdong.

Other Circumstances

The airplane numbered sixteen was severely damaged, the fuselage completely unusable, but the engine is still usable. The company has sent craftsmen to dismantle it and transport it to Shanghai. As for the injured pilot and passengers, except for two who have been bandaged and discharged from the hospital, the others are still in Hong'en Hospital for treatment. The treatment is progressing very well. Although the co-pilot, the American Aimo, has both legs broken, it can be assured that there is no danger to his life.

Reasons for the Drop in Standard Yarn Prices

According to the Central News Agency, since the Cotton Control Association took measures to stabilize yarn prices in order to relieve yarn mills and promote sales, yarn sales have been smooth. Unexpectedly, the price of November standard yarn on the Yarn Exchange suddenly dropped by six yuan at the last moment, surprising everyone. The truth is tentatively explored as follows: The standard yarn samples stored by the Cotton Control Association at the Yarn Exchange are of too low quality, giving manufacturers the opportunity to submit inferior yarn. The validity period of these standard yarn samples is due to expire at the end of this year. For emergency purposes, the Ministry of Industry is requested to instruct the exchange to suspend the acceptance of new yarn submissions in November and December to reduce harm to the yarn industry. The exchange, being a speculative market, then had some people organize a bull company, buying November and December standard yarn, unaware that the yarn prices in the Yarn Exchange in November and December were only sufficient to replace a batch of accumulated inferior yarn. The bull company, unaware, raised the price, causing the standard price to exceed the current selling price of inferior yarn on the market by four or five yuan. Who knew that on the last day of bidding for November standard yarn, the bull company suddenly disintegrated for some reason, selling all of its more than ten thousand pieces of goods in one day, resulting in a sharp drop of six yuan in standard yarn prices. Now, starting from December, standard yarn prices have stabilized and are equal to the current spot prices on the market.

Ministry of Finance and Tax Administration Cancels Ban on Rice and Wheat Exports; Bran Cannot Be Handled Similarly

The Shanghai Flour Milling Industry Association previously stated that the excessive surplus of agricultural products in various regions directly affected prices. To seek relief, they requested the Tax Administration to allow the export of wheat flour. The Tax Administration has now approved the request. The original approval is recorded below. The case of banning the export of wheat flour was originally due to domestic disasters and insufficient food supply at the time, and this Ministry was ordered to handle it. Now the situation of excessive surplus of agricultural products in various regions is the opposite of the previous situation. The request to allow the export of No. 2, 3, and 4 wheat flour can be approved. However, wheat flour is not subject to customs duties. The current tax is still a special tax, which is clearly different from other grains that are subject to customs duties. It should not be completely exempt from tax. The special tax on wheat flour should still be collected according to the regulations. After export, half of the actual tax amount should be refunded to comply with the regulations and encourage exports. As for bran, it is mostly an industrial product, with large annual exports, and has never been banned. Its nature is different from that of grain, so it is difficult to grant the same tax exemption. Moreover, the Association submitted a request for tax exemption on bran exports in July of this year, which was disapproved by this Ministry. It should be handled accordingly. In addition to forwarding the report and issuing orders, this approval is for your information.

Xin-yi and others were ordered to be responsible for preparation and should comply with the instructions. Fisheries Administration to Close at the End of the Month; Establishment of a Fish Market Difficult to Realize for the Time Being

According to the Central News Agency, after the central government approved the temporary closure of the fisheries administrations in various regions, the Jiangzhe District Fisheries Administration in this port received instructions from the Ministry of Industry a few days ago to handle the closure. It is understood that the reason for the closure is related to the collection of fisheries construction fees. After the closure of the bureau, all its work will be handled directly by the Ministry of Industry. The details are as follows:

Deadline for Closure: After receiving the order to close the Jiangzhe District Fisheries Administration, the director of the bureau, Yuan Ji, ordered all staff to handle the closure. The Ministry order originally limited the bureau to close at the end of the month. Now the deadline is approaching, and most of the work can be completed. For other trivial matters that cannot be completed in time, a small number of staff will be temporarily retained to continue handling them.

Reasons for Closure: According to Wu Huanru, a member of the Fisheries Improvement Committee, speaking to a reporter from the Central News Agency, although fisheries construction is important, there are many businesses to be developed, and it is difficult to achieve them due to limited funds. As for the collection of fisheries construction fees, if implemented, it would be difficult to use them all for fisheries construction. The authorities had promised that after collecting fisheries construction fees, all ship donations and other miscellaneous donations in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai would be waived. The three provinces and cities of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai would need to allocate more than 100,000 yuan from the fisheries construction fee revenue to compensate for the exemption of fishing boat donations. In addition, after deducting expenses such as ocean protection, the remaining tens of thousands of yuan would be insufficient to develop the fisheries construction industry. Therefore, the central government decided to close the Fisheries Improvement Committee and the Fisheries Construction Fee Collection Office, as there was no need to establish them. The business and expenses of the Fisheries Administration could not be planned, and it was decided to temporarily suspend them.

Future Plans: Wu also said that the Ministry of Industry will continue to handle the passive aspect of ocean protection and plans to jointly establish a fish market between the central government and the city. The Ministry of Industry and the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau have sent personnel to Nagasaki, Japan, and Qingdao, China, to visit fish markets for reference. They have recently returned to Shanghai and will submit a detailed report. Whether the government will operate it or whether it will be jointly operated by the government and merchants has not yet been determined. Recently, a preparatory committee will be organized to plan everything. The market will be located in the coastal area of the city, with a capital of more than one million yuan. However, there is no funding for the capital yet.

Farmers in Gaoqiao District Petition for Permanent Tenancy Rights in Jiangxinsha

More than 700 acres of land in Daxi Dang, Jiangxinsha, Tu 27, Gaoqiao District of this city, were invested in by farmers from Chongming around 1924 and obtained permanent tenancy rights. After years of hard work, the land was finally cultivated, and they divided the harvest with the landlord at a ratio of 4:6, living in peace. Unexpectedly, the landlord, Hu Rongcao of Daxingzhuang, suddenly sold all the cultivated land in the area to Lever Brothers, a British company, this autumn to build an oil field, earning hundreds of thousands of yuan and disregarding the lives of hundreds of farmers in the area. He even threatened to demolish the thatched huts and expel them. The farmers in each morning took their lives, and since they had obtained permanent tenancy rights, they decided not to let the landlord sell it privately. At 2:00 yesterday afternoon, they jointly sent representatives from the entire area, including Huang Zhirong, Shi Tingtong, Geng Xinggao, Jin Genggen, Song Dalang, Ding Wangfu, Dong Ergou, Huang Youcai, Zhang Qiaofu, and more than 40 others, to the city party headquarters and the city council to petition. Lu Yinchu, a cadre from the Civil Training Section of the City Party Headquarters, received them and promised to investigate and handle the matter. Yu Zhenhui, a member of the Standing Committee of the City Farmers Association, received them and promised to handle the matter together with the City Party Headquarters in accordance with the law. The representatives were satisfied and left.

Jianghai Customs Announces Goods Grading Method

City merchants received a notice from Jianghai Customs stating that regarding the taxation of goods according to value grades as stipulated in the tariff, the method of grading goods has now been issued to the customs by government order and is recorded below: (1) For imported goods that are taxed separately according to the value grades stipulated in the light tariff, the value shall be regarded as the duty-paying price in Section 1 of Article 1 of the Provisional Regulations on Import Tariffs. When this value grade is compared with the wholesale market price of the goods, the following shall be added: (A) the tax rate, (B) the current surtax, and (C) 7% of the price, converted to the wholesale market price grade. (2) If the wholesale market price of the goods is within a certain grade range of the wholesale market price converted according to the value stipulated in the tariff in accordance with item 1, the tax rate of that grade shall be applied. (3) If the wholesale market price of the goods is between two grades of the wholesale market price converted according to the value stipulated in the tariff in item 1, it shall be classified into the closer grade for taxation. It is understood that the association has notified the industry associations of the situation.

Increased Water Transport Costs Due to River Closure in North China

The weather in North China has been severely cold recently, and Yingkou and Tianjin have already had snowfall. After the Taikoo steamer "Daming" sailed to Niuzhuang last Saturday, the shipping companies in this port will no longer send ships to Yingkou this year due to the impending freezing. As for Tianjin, the date of river closure is also approaching. Starting from December 1st, the shipping companies in Shanghai to Tianjin have already publicly discussed increasing the water transport costs for the ice river yesterday. For foreign cloth and cotton yarn, an additional 1% will be charged according to the fixed rate, and for various groceries, an additional 20% will be charged according to the original amount. However, whether to increase the cost for flour has not yet been decided. Yesterday, the companies notified the customers in North China to take note.

Li Delie Returns to Australia

According to the China Mail, the Australian Li Delie came to China 47 years ago and initially served in the Jiujiang Church. The current Western residential area of Guling was purchased and developed by Li on that day. In 1900, he joined the Shanghai Brunner Mond & Co., Ltd. At that time, annual sales were less than 200 tons, but by the time Li left the company in 1919, it had increased to more than 40,000 tons. From 1904 to 1906, he served as a director of the Shanghai Municipal Council. In 1912, the Wuchang Uprising broke out, and then Wu Tingfang and Tang Shaoyi of the North and South factions negotiated a peace. Li mediated between them, and the meeting place was Li's residence on Gordon Road. After all matters were agreed upon, a public meeting was held at the old council hall on Nanjing Road, where the conditions were signed, and Puyi abdicated. After leaving Brunner Mond & Co., Ltd., Li served as the first Australian Commercial Commissioner to China for two and a half years. Later, the position was abolished, and Li lived in New South Wales, but still occasionally came to China for short trips. He recently returned to Shanghai and, tired of traveling, will return to Australia with his wife today (the 28th). Li recently celebrated his 70th birthday.

Xiang-E Road: Xujiapeng Joins the Intermodal Transport Station

The Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Bureaus both announced that the Traffic Department of the Xiang-E Railway Bureau recently stated that although Xujiapeng Station on the line is only separated from Hankou by a river and only has ferry transportation, it is inconvenient for passengers in the Wuchang area to move their luggage across the river. In order to serve the community, with the consent of the Intermodal Transport Department of the Ministry of Railways, Xujiapeng Station will be added to the intermodal transport station from now on to facilitate business travelers. The mileage and fares are as follows: The distance between Hankou and Xujiapeng is ten kilometers, and the ferry fee is 15 cents for first class, 10 cents for second class, and 5 cents for third class.

Xu Leqing Kidnapping Case: Two Kidnappers Sentenced to Death, Wu Ziqiu and Others Sentenced to Various Terms of Imprisonment

Xu Leqing, a broker at the Cloth Exchange, was walking from his residence to Haig Road in Jing'an Temple on September 1st of this year when he was attacked by kidnappers. When the attempt to kidnap him failed, they shot and killed him. The General Inspectorate and the Zhabei Police Station, led by Chinese Inspector Lu Liankui, Chief Inspector You Agen, and Inspectors Liu Shaokui and Dong Zhaobin, successively arrested ten kidnappers involved in the case, including Wu Youshan, Wu Ziqiu, Wang Laojiu, and Yao Zhifa, and sent them to the First Special Court. After repeated hearings, it was found that the defendants, in addition to kidnapping and killing Xu Leqing, had also kidnapped Shen Jixiu and others in Pingle Lane, Jiujiang Road, on April 22nd. After a debate, the defendants Gu Dakang (i.e., Ren San) and Dong Zilian were released on bail, and the others were detained. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the sentencing of this case. The lawyer for Gu, Hong Shihao, and the lawyer for Dong, Ye Fubang, were present in court to await instructions. At 2:30, Judge Wu Tingqi ascended to the eighth criminal court and announced the verdict. The main text stated: Yao Zhifa was sentenced to death for the crime of jointly kidnapping and extortion, and sentenced to death for the crime of jointly murdering. He was sentenced to life imprisonment for the crime of helping kidnap and extort. The death penalty was executed. Wang Laojiu was sentenced to two death sentences for the crime of helping kidnap and extort in two instances, and sentenced to twelve years in prison for the crime of helping kidnap and extort in an attempted crime. The death penalty was executed, and the rest of the charges were dismissed. Wu Ziqiu was sentenced to twenty years in prison for the crime of helping kidnap and extort. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized was equivalent to one day of imprisonment for every two days. The rest of the charges were dismissed. Wu Youshan was sentenced to twelve years in prison for the crime of helping kidnap and extort. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized was equivalent to one day of imprisonment for every two days. The rest of the charges were dismissed. Zhang Desheng and Wang Asan were each sentenced to twelve years in prison for the crime of helping kidnap and extort. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized was equivalent to one day of imprisonment for every two days. The rest of the charges were dismissed. Two pistols, three magazines, fifty bullets, one bullet head, and one cartridge case, as well as a No. 6669 car, a No. Huang car driver's uniform, and a hat were confiscated. Gu Dakang, Hua Gongnan, Dong Zilian, and Liu Fusheng were all found not guilty. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, rose and requested that Liu Fusheng be allowed to be returned to custody during the appeal period. The court approved it.

Italian electrical engineer Guglielmo Marconi, famous worldwide for his invention of wireless telegraphy, is touring the Far East with his wife. After resting in Beijing, he will travel directly to Nanjing by train on December 7th and arrive in Shanghai on the Shanghai-Nanjing train on the 8th. He will stay in Shanghai for several days and depart on the Conte Rosso on the 12th.

Guomin News Agency reports that silk merchants Sheng Jisheng and Cheng Jingpo from Hangzhou and Huzhou, recognizing that the massive dumping of foreign artificial silk into China in recent years has clearly defeated our country's natural silk, causing the silk industry to decline sharply and the unemployed workers to suffer greatly, have therefore gathered many colleagues and contacted financial giants in Shanghai to create a large-scale artificial silk factory themselves, to reverse profit rights and promote domestic goods. Pudong Three Districts Advance Winter Defense

Zhang Mingqin, the district chief of the third district of the Pudong Public Security Bureau, believing that this year's winter defense should be implemented earlier than in previous years due to the current situation, in order to maintain public order, convened local police and regimental officers to the district for a meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday morning. Attendees included the heads of the 1st, 2nd, 3rd, 4th, and 5th branch stations, Yuan, the captain of the second police detachment, Xu, the head of the security corps, Xia Xinzai, the director of the Chamber of Commerce, and Jiang Wende, the director of the Fire Brigade. Chairman Zhang reported first, briefly stating that due to the recent Fujian Incident, winter defense matters should be implemented early. Residents in various places are increasing in number, and they are of varying quality, so we should pay more attention to them. Subsequently, the people present expressed their opinions and discussed the results, and the main points of the discussion were as follows: (1) The first step is to establish a joint police and regimental winter defense association, with the office set up in the third district office, and the funds will be subsidized by the business community. (2) Establish a joint whistleblowing method between the district and the station and between the stations to respond to each other. (3) Select various important locations such as Qinci Yangdian and Tuditang to set up observation posts to communicate news. (4) The Pudong Avenue is dozens of miles long, connecting the jurisdiction of the first district and five branch stations. There are many pedestrians, but it is still very deserted on both sides, so it should be valued. The third district should submit a request to the General Bureau to allocate two mechanical bicycles to patrol back and forth at any time to ensure security and peace. (5) Each branch station should select busy and quiet places to appropriately increase the number of bicycle police to patrol back and forth to strengthen defense. (6) The police and regiment will jointly check the passengers getting on and off the ferries at various ports at any time. (7) Check the household registration at any time. (8) The security corps members should step up night defense to supplement insufficient police force. (9) Fire Brigade members should be ready to be dispatched at any time in the evening. The discussion ended at noon and the meeting adjourned.

Animal Hibernation, City Zoo Opens Greenhouse, Hibiscus Competition Registration Closes Tomorrow

The Municipal Zoo of this city, due to the gradually colder weather and animal hibernation, has opened the greenhouse. The registration for the Hibiscus Competition will close tomorrow. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Animal Hibernation Starts Using Greenhouse

The zoo, considering that the weather is getting colder and the animal hibernation season has arrived, such as reptiles and amphibians, have all stopped moving. Therefore, the hot water radiator laid by the zoo has been used every night starting yesterday to keep the temperature in the animal house moderate to maintain their lives. If the weather gets colder, the greenhouse will be used day and night.

Hibiscus Competition Registration Deadline

Since the start of soliciting, the Hibiscus Competition held by the zoo has received enthusiastic registrations from Chinese and Westerners. Registration will close on the 30th of this month. It is estimated that more than 70 people and more than hundreds of hibiscus will participate in this event. The number of German species and Chinese species is equal, followed by British species and Dutch species, and mixed species. In total, foreign species are more numerous than domestic species.

Scheduled Opening to Invite Reporters

The Hibiscus Competition is scheduled to open on December 10th. The judges have already been hired. In order to expand publicity and encourage the breeding of songbirds, the zoo will specially invite reporters from various newspapers to visit and conduct public reviews on the opening day. In order to limit the number of spectators, admission tickets will be charged.

Crowds of Tourists Vie to See Large Tortoises

Since the zoo purchased a large tortoise from the Philippines and displayed a pair of bats, the number of tourists has doubled in recent days. However, the circumference of this tortoise is less than one square foot, which is quite different from the reported three feet long and two feet wide (Shanghai News Agency).

China Foreign Famine Relief Association Holds Yellow River Disaster Relief Near News

The Shanghai office of the China Foreign Famine Relief Association at No. 49 Nanjing Road, Public Concession, received a telegram from the Beijing General Association yesterday, reporting that at the 124th Executive Committee meeting held on the 22nd of this month, a resolution was passed to send personnel to the Yellow River flood disaster areas in various provinces to start agricultural relief work and allocate all current donations.

Inspector of the Yellow River Disaster Relief Committee Reports on the Situation of Providing Congee in Shandong

The disaster relief group of the Yellow River Flood Relief Committee previously sent an employee, Shi Xuan, to inspect the disaster and relief work in Hebei, Shandong, and Henan. The committee received Shi Xuan's report yesterday on the inspection of the investigation office and the operation of the congee factory in Shandong. It generally stated that the work of the investigation office was carried out in a very organized manner and the external impression was also very good. There are currently seven congee factories set up, established in areas with a relatively large number of victims. Each factory provides congee for 2,000 people. The congee provision is divided into two methods: (1) distribution under normal circumstances; (2) distribution of relief grain. The second item is a flexible method based on the situation. Because many victims prefer to receive congee and grain at home and cook it with taro and beans at any time, it is more filling and convenient than going to the factory to eat or receiving congee at home, especially when the weather is cold and the road is far away. Therefore, those who are allowed to receive dry food will receive it once every ten days, calculated on a daily basis, and the congee and grain will be paid to them for self-cooking. The factory can also save a lot of fuel, and the remaining money will be used to purchase rice and grain to increase the number of eaters. A complaint box is also set up for eaters to contribute their opinions. The congee provided is requested by health personnel to inspect nearby at any time to avoid unsanitary and other malpractices.

Charity Federation Raises Funds for Winter Shelters

The Shanghai Charity Federation held a meeting at 4:00 PM the day before yesterday. Attendees included Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Chen Liangyu representing Pushan Villa, Wu Shutian representing Shanghai Charity Group, Wang Zhongfu representing Guangyi Shantang and China Relief for Women and Children Association, Huang Juntang representing Weizhong Shantang, Weng Yin first representing Lianyi Shantang and Lianyi Branch, Chen Wenkui representing Shanghai Disabled Persons' Hospital, Sun Yishan representing Hunan Zishan Society, Zhang Junkang representing Shanghai Orphanage, Qi Taofu representing Baoan Nursing Home, Fang Zhijun representing Renji Shantang, Chen Kaifeng representing Renji Infant Nursery, and Huang Hanzhi representing Xinwei Relief Society. Chairman Wang Yiting first reported that the association has been setting up temporary winter shelters every year to accommodate civilians. Now that winter is approaching and severe cold is coming, at this time when rural areas are bankrupt and all industries are depressed, the number of civilians who are hungry, cold, displaced, and unable to support themselves must be greater than in previous years. Winter shelters should be opened earlier. The Social Bureau has also sent a letter urging us, but the funds for the winter shelters are not specific and rely entirely on temporary fundraising. In the current social situation, fundraising is not guaranteed. Each charity group has annual donations, and this year's situation is more difficult, especially hoping for efforts to donate to cope with it. It was decided that the economic conditions of each charity group have been difficult in recent years, and assistance should be provided for the funds of the winter shelters. Mr. Wang Yiting recognized a donation of 100 yuan, Mr. Huang Hanzhi recognized a donation of 100 yuan, and Mr. Wu Shutian recognized a donation of 50 yuan. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Tianzhang West Factory Labor Strike, General Labor Union Mediates Resumption of Work, Both Parties Sign 11 Reconciliation Terms

The workers of Tianzhang Paper West Factory on Yangshupu Road and Dong Factory in Lujia Crossing, Pudong, were triggered by the employer's failure to pay wages on time, causing repercussions. Therefore, they were unwilling to fulfill the reconciliation record of the Social Bureau, resulting in a strike that has lasted for six days. The Municipal General Labor Union paid extraordinary attention to this dispute. Yesterday afternoon, the union invited labor and management representatives to mediate again. Both parties decided on 11 reconciliation terms, and the labor side has approved the resumption of work this morning (29th). As for the Dong Factory, it is scheduled to continue negotiations today. The attached reconciliation terms are as follows: (1) 20 workers will be dismissed, and each will be given dismissal pay, calculated as 60 days of wages. (2) Wages will be temporarily deducted by 20%, according to the reconciliation record of the Social Bureau. (3) Half of the wages will be paid during the strike period. (4) Wages will be paid on time as scheduled. (5) Those who do not ask for leave each month will receive a wage increase of two days at the end of the month. Those who ask for one day of personal leave will receive a wage increase of one day. Those who ask for two days of personal leave will not receive an increase. (6) Regardless of the company's profit or loss at the end of the year, all bonuses will be issued, calculated as 20 days of wages. (7) The wages for commemorative days will be handled in accordance with government laws and regulations. (8) Two days per month will be used for parking and repairs. The dates will be determined by the company. Workers must complete the repairs before leaving the factory. (9) Workers who ask for leave due to illness must provide proof from a doctor or hospital designated by the company, and wages will be paid as usual. The payment method will be handled in accordance with the factory law. (10) All workers must re-fill out application forms. (11) Workers may not be dismissed without reason. If they are dismissed, they must be handled in accordance with the previous regulations. Those who do not comply with the factory rules will not receive dismissal pay. It is heard that the reconciliation terms will be submitted to the party and government organs for record.

Wang Xiaolai and Du Yuesheng Mediate the Sanyou Case, Hope for Resolution

According to the New Sound Society, the Shanghai Local Court recently entrusted the Special District Local Court to enforce the Sanyou Industrial Society's dismissal of workers at the Sanyou Yinxiang Factory case. It is heard that there are indeed practical difficulties in this case. Currently, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai and Supervisory Committee Member Du Yuesheng are trying to mediate. They discussed until 2 a.m. the other day and have reached a considerable solution. The employer is being persuaded by Wang Xiaolai, and the labor side by Du Yuesheng. A preliminary agreement has also been reached on the amount of severance pay.

Wusong Chamber of Commerce Requests Return of Funds Advanced by Merchants and Residents During Wartime; Year-End Approaching; Hoping for Reimbursement

During the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the Wusong Chamber of Commerce office supplied military needs, soliciting and advancing funds from various businesses for military use and maintaining public order. The amount was considerable. It has been two years, and the Chamber of Commerce has once urged the authorities to reimburse the funds, but they have not been returned. Now, with the Wusong area's market depressed and the year-end approaching, they hope for reimbursement as eagerly as for rain. Several businesses are waiting for these funds to be repaid to settle debts. After the Wusong Eighth District Party Department sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce, the Chamber yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce requesting it to find a way to allocate the funds before the end of the year to alleviate the merchants' difficulties.
