Cigarette Paper Shop Exchanges Counterfeit Silver Coins, Fang Zhengwu Wrongly Detained for One Day

Fang Zhengwu, who resides at No. 5 Yongxiangfang, Tongfu Road and works in a foreign firm, recently passed by Fuyou Road in the city and exchanged five yuan in banknotes for one yuan in silver coins at Qingchengfeng Cigarette Paper Shop at No. 419. He received four yuan in silver dollars, six double coins, and fifteen copper coins. He took them elsewhere. When passing Xiaonanmen, he needed change and exchanged one silver dollar for coins at a cigarette paper shop there. Unexpectedly, it was discovered to be a counterfeit silver dollar. Fang immediately argued that it was exchanged at Fuyou Road. The shop did not believe him and searched him, finding another counterfeit silver dollar among the remaining three yuan. Accused of using counterfeit silver dollars, the police from the post detained him in the First District and First Precinct for investigation. Fortunately, Fang knew Chief Hong of the Second Section and was able to prove his innocence and was released, but he had been wrongly detained for one day. Yesterday at 5:20 p.m., Fang used a five-yuan transit ticket, with a secret mark of the character "Lu" on the ticket, and went to Qingchengfeng Cigarette Paper Shop to exchange for coins again. The shop still gave him two yuan in counterfeit silver dollars, two yuan in good silver dollars, six double coins, and fifteen copper coins. As soon as Fang saw the counterfeit silver dollars, he immediately questioned the shop, but the shop denied it, saying it was a switch. Therefore, Fang called Fan Delin from the 17th post to come. Because there was no evidence, he immediately called the precinct to report the matter and asked for a team to come and search. Unexpectedly, at this moment, the shop owner and others escaped in the meantime. Only two shop assistants were arrested. Patrol Captain Li Fuyi found thirty-five silver dollars (the counterfeit silver dollars among them were difficult to identify), twenty-eight yuan in banknotes, seventy-one cents in coin tickets, seven hundred forty-four good double coins, six hundred thirty-two Shantou coins, seventy new coins, one hundred seventy-four private plates, eighteen lead coins, thirty-two single coins, and twenty damaged single coins in a wooden comb box in the shop. They were all detained for investigation. According to Liu, the precinct chief, the defendant, Zhang Lixuan, 19 years old, from Shaoxing, a clerk at Qingchengfeng, and another named Chen Nian, 35 years old, from Shaoxing, who left Qingchengfeng shop, claimed that the boss had fled and they did not know anything about the shop. They were sent to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau for legal action.

How Did Female Worker Bian Zhaoyou Die? The Court Must Find a Way to Re-examine

Bian Yonggen, 30 years old, from Shaoxing, residing at No. 43 Wuhuali, Huade Road, Hongkou, works as a carpenter for a living. He has a niece named Bian Zhaoyou, 16 years old. Because of the hard life in the countryside, she came to Shanghai last spring and was introduced to work at the Shenxin Yarn Factory in Zhoujiaqiao, West Shanghai. For the convenience of going back and forth, she lived in the boarding house opened by her fellow villager Zhang Qian at No. 71 Shenxin Workers' Quarters near the factory. The girl could earn more than ten yuan a month. After deducting the cost of food, she could save several yuan a month. She had been working diligently for more than a year and a half. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday, her uncle Bian Yonggen suddenly received a report that his niece Zhaoyou had been abused and beaten to death by the owner of the boarding house, Zhang Qian, and had been dead for several days and had not yet been placed in a coffin. Bian was shocked and immediately rushed to the scene. Sure enough, he saw that his niece's body was still there. Bian then twisted the owner of the boarding house, Zhang Qian, to the Chenjiadu Sixth District Police Station, and transferred her to the Sixth District, accusing her of murdering someone. After receiving the report, District Chief Tan ordered the map and land guard to report to the local court for an examination. Yesterday, the court appointed Inspector Yang to inspect the scene. It was examined that the female corpse had been dead for about ten days. The skin was swollen and another method was needed for detailed examination. Therefore, he returned to the court without examining. Then, District Officer Xing interrogated and recorded the statement of the plaintiff Bian Yonggen, and also the statement of the defendant Zhang Qian, 32 years old, from Shaoxing, who runs a boarding house in Shenxin Workers' Quarters. She said that after the girl Zhaoyou lived in the boarding house last year, she treated her very well. Now she suddenly died of a sha disease. She had asked Chinese and Western doctors in the factory to diagnose her and take medicine, and there was no abuse or beating. After getting the statements, the district officer temporarily detained her because the case involved a life. After the investigation is clear, and the court re-examines, it will be handled after verification.

Investigation and Detention for Selling Counterfeit Cigarettes

Lu Changsheng, the chief detective of the interview department of the French Concession Police Department, received a secret report the day before yesterday, stating that Wang Binghe (26 years old), a native of Yong, who lives at No. 69 Hongyuan Lane, Huade Road, Hongkou, has recently been privately manufacturing counterfeit "Dazhongnan" and "Fairy" brand cigarettes and selling them to famous cigarette paper shops for profit. At noon today, Wang carried cigarettes to various cigarette paper shops near the Great World to sell them. The detective immediately accompanied detective Chen Yishan and the informant to wait at the entrance of the Great World. At 12:30 p.m., Wang was seen walking slowly with a paper bag. He was immediately detained and the paper bag was opened. Inside were fifty packs of "Dazhongnan" and "Fairy" brand 20-cigarette packs, totaling one thousand cigarettes. He was taken to the police station. According to Wang's confession, the manufacturing facility was located at his home at No. 69 Hongyuan Lane, Huade Road. The detectives then took Wang to the Yulin Road Police Station to report the incident and asked for detectives to go with them to search. Xia Shuxiang, a native of Zhenjiang who co-owned the business with Wang, was seen working on rolling cigarettes in the back room of the reception hall. He was immediately arrested and 5,000 counterfeit cigarettes, about 3,000 sheets of cigarette paper, about ten kilograms of tobacco, three seals used on cigarette packs (Dazhongnan and Fairy, both in Chinese and Western characters), and items used for rolling cigarettes were confiscated. They were all brought back to the police station and sent to the Second Special District Court yesterday. At 3 p.m., Judge Sun Pengxian tried the case in the Eighth Criminal Court. First, the police lawyer Yao Zhaodi explained the case and requested a postponement for further investigation and interrogation, and presented the evidence to the court. Shen Wenjie, an employee of the Zhongnan Cigarette Company, and lawyer Li Pengcheng came to the court, requesting to bring a private prosecution to recover losses. Wang and Xia, the two defendants, confessed to privately manufacturing counterfeit cigarettes as a joint venture. The judge ordered the defendants to be taken back into custody pending further trial.

Assassination of Candle Shop Owner; Accomplices Escorted from Ningbo to Shanghai for Trial

Chen Chukui, 29 years old, a native of Ningbo and the owner of Qianfengtai Candle Shop at No. 51 and 52 Xinqiao Street in the French Concession, was shot in the throat by thugs on April 29th of this year at about 8 p.m. when he returned to the store from outside and detoured to the small alley next door. At the same time, Chen Qiancheng, the manager of the store, heard the sound and went out to rescue him, but was also injured. (According to reports, the two thugs borrowed two pistols from Wang Liutang, a tenant in Chen's pavilion room, and went downstairs. They happened to meet Chen in the alley and questioned him. The thugs, fearing that things would go wrong, took out their guns to resist, resulting in a major disaster.) Later, the French Concession Police Department arrested the murderer Zhu Quanxing, a native of Wuxi (20 years old, living at No. 40 Shungui Lane, Father Du Road, the younger brother of Luo Zhutourong, a member of the flower club), and found two pistols and several bullets in the grass pile in the cemetery of the Siming Guild Hall outside the back door of No. 7 Yuqing Lane, Baliao Bridge Road. He was sent to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. Zhu was sentenced to 15 years in prison for murder. Zhu refused to accept the original judgment and appealed to the Third High Court. The case is currently being heard. According to Zhu, his accomplice Chen Jinlan, a native of Yong, nicknamed Snake Skin, 31 years old, had been investigated by the police department and found to have fled to the Ningbo countryside. A warrant was specially issued by the Second Special Court, and a document was sent to the Ningbo Public Security Bureau, requesting assistance in the arrest. Chen has now been arrested by the local Public Security Bureau, and the French Concession Police Department has been notified to send detectives to Ningbo to escort him back. He arrived in Shanghai by steamer yesterday morning and was brought to the police station. He was immediately transferred to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District. Judge Wang Gangxu interrogated him. According to the police lawyer Gu Shouxi, the police department has clearly stated the case and requested that the defendant be taken into custody and postponed for two weeks for a detailed investigation of the case before filing a lawsuit. After verifying the report, the court asked the defendant for a statement and then ordered a postponement to December 12 for further trial. The defendant was taken back into custody.

Young Woman Abducted and Sold into Prostitution by Villains

Zhu Hongbao, a woman, is now 20 years old, from Wuzhen, Zhejiang Province. She has a beautiful appearance and is extremely promiscuous. Two years ago, in August, she married Lu Ada, who worked as a barge operator, through a matchmaker. Lu made a living by boat, and due to life problems, he could not often accompany his beautiful wife to enjoy the fun of the boudoir. Therefore, he often made Hong sell the empty boudoir and stay alone, lamenting her bitter fate. Soon Zhu became acquainted with a Lu Abao. Lu was in his prime and was able to win Zhu's heart, living together like a couple. In the summer of this year, Lu Abao lured Zhu with sweet words, saying how prosperous Shanghai was and that it would be good to take a trip. If she could marry a wealthy husband, she would not have to worry about eating for the rest of her life. The woman was tempted by his words and came to Shanghai with him, staying at the Sihai Hotel on Tianjin Road. Letter

Dear Editor, I have just read a news item in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on the 28th of this month about a false fire alarm, which stated, "Up and down, I have no choice but to be crowded, and the door is narrow, and I am crowded. More than a dozen workers with weak strength were crowded and fell to the ground and were trampled, etc." After investigation, the roads, Zhou gates and households in our factory are extremely wide, and have been approved by the concession engineering bureau and the fire brigade, pointing out that they meet the factory building. The narrow door and so on in your newspaper are probably rumors. For this reason, please correct it. Sincerely, Shanghai Guangdong Brothers Rubber Manufacturing Company General Distributor, November 28.

Occasional Pieces

No Point in Discussing What's Done

— 19

"No point in discussing what's done" is a sage's teaching. This saying has been deeply rooted in people's hearts for thousands of years. Leaving aside other matters, preventing fights is a common example. Ah Mao from the Zhang family got beaten up by Zhao Di from the Li family. Naturally, Ah Mao would run back with snot and tears to tell his mother. What would his mother do? She would inevitably feel sorry for him, but thinking of "golden neighbors, silver relatives," she would have to suppress her anger. Moreover, the two families were neighbors, always visiting each other. Mrs. Li went to the market with her every morning and visited the Great World entertainment center every night. Could they fall out over such a small matter? Even Ah Mao's father, returning from his foreign firm and learning of this, would praise his wife's ability to maintain overall harmony. The reason is that the fight has already happened. Since it's a done deal, even scolding is useless. It's better to let it go and avoid hurting the relationship. This is the result of the sage's teachings deeply rooted in people's hearts.

"Moderation and Harmony" are the foundation of cultivating oneself, managing one's family, governing the state, and bringing peace to the world in our country. "Moderation is the universal path; harmony is the great foundation of the world." This is an indirect sage's teaching. "Moderation and Harmony" have such great power, so China has been able to turn danger into safety and safety into danger, not least because the people possess this virtue. This may seem to drift further and further away, but if one carefully examines the meaning of "no point in discussing what's done," doesn't it conform to "moderation" and "harmony"? How do foreign mothers deal with their children fighting? I haven't had the good fortune to marry a foreign wife, nor have I been abroad, so I dare not make assumptions. However, the virtues of foreigners can never match the moderation and harmony of our people. Based on this, perhaps the mother of a foreign "Ah Mao" would not let it go. To us Chinese, this would be criticizing them for not knowing the big picture. But we must forgive them because they have never read the sage's teaching of "no point in discussing what's done."

Some Thoughts

— Qian Jian

On the bustling Jing'an Temple Road, motorcycles sped by like lightning, constantly moving. The rumbling trams crawled along the tracks, going back and forth. And the intense sounds of motor vehicles and bicycles, the horns of motorcycles, and the noise of various sounds showed full joy, pleasure, and prosperity.

On one side of the sidewalk, a black door was lazily half-open. Walking from the door to the inside, two rows of tall maple trees, blown by the autumn wind, screamed wildly, their leaves flying piece by piece onto the pavement and the cemetery with crosses. And the amiable god of love, with a long leaf in his hand, did show unusual depression, loneliness, and coldness. || It turned out that this was the site of a foreign cemetery. Crosses were scattered everywhere, standing unevenly. At the same time, various colorful flowers also caught the eye: this has already proven that they (or she/they) are silent and have passed away.

In one corner, marble and iron railings surrounded his perimeter, the stone emitting a bright reflection. The god of love amiably stood by his side. On the tombstone, lines of gold letters were engraved, listing his life's history, the dates of his death, and the age he enjoyed. Moreover, a magnetic photo of his plump face and昂昻气概 was embedded on the tombstone. And beautiful flowers were placed before his spirit, emitting a rich fragrance to comfort his soul; lush trees surrounded his perimeter, releasing fresh air, as if to comfort his body and mind. Alas! How glorious they are!

In another corner, only a black wooden cross stood askew, the grave overgrown with weeds and withered grass, covered with fragments of broken bottles and scattered tiles. Even a clump of grass indicated the resting place of the deceased's soul. Alas! How lonely and desolate they are!

From this, we can imagine the glory and pleasure of the deceased's life from the exquisite equipment on the grave. At the same time, if there is only a desolate grave as the resting place for the ghost, then we can also imagine the poverty and suffering of the deceased before.

Alas! The glorious are glorious and enjoy themselves after death; the poor are poor and suffer after death.

Alas! If there is a soul after death, then the generally dead poor may have to weep bitterly!

Believe it or Not

— Jin Jia

Generally speaking, those who achieve great things in the world are often not the darlings of the goddess of fortune, but rather those "without opportunity," the poor children.

The extent of your achievement will never exceed the extent of your self-confidence.

The refinement or coarseness, superiority or inferiority of your conversation best reveals your level of education and social worth.

Economic distress, business failure, and difficult living are when "real people" make the greatest progress.

If a person often thinks that they are not capable enough to succeed, then there is no reason for them to succeed.

Starting from Fearing One's Wife

— Lian Lian

Generally, a person develops a fear of something or a situation because the other party has the motivation to be feared and threatened. Whether or not the fear will inevitably occur depends on one's courage and bravery. However, it is said that there are very, very few men who marry a wife and are not afraid of her.

I have many classmates who, before they got married, were fully heroic youths. Whether they said a word or did something, they were always high-spirited, intense, and self-centered. When they occasionally talked about women, they smiled dismissively, as if they were unworthy of study. As for saying that men are afraid of their wives, they didn't believe it one hundred and twenty percent. They would say, "What are we men afraid of? Are we worthy of being great men if we cower before women?" Their words were certainly beautiful and straightforward, but after they got married, when I asked them again, they were all silent. They didn't say anything more, just said faintly: "How many men in the world are not afraid of their wives?"

Originally, heroes have difficulty getting past the beauty trap. The ancients had already said this. But I don't know how Napoleon in the past and Hitler today treated their wives in foreign countries.

"Hedong Lion's Roar" is originally the tone used by those who fear their wives to describe the wife's mighty power. The lion is the king of beasts, and its subjugation of the wolves is only in one roar. However, comparing one's wife to a lion and willingly becoming a follower completely exposes one's pitiful and laughable attitude.

But speaking seriously, under the current atmosphere of high Chinese women's rights, a woman who can recognize her own position and rise up to do something great has a better chance and hope of success than a man. The lion symbolizes China. If the lion can wake up and roar, there may be hope for the future. But it sleeps soundly, without any consciousness. As for the Hedong Lion, it only roars in the house. So-called women's rights are only like this. To be like Lin Yutang's so-called "let the women do it for a while," then the Hedong Lion should turn around, step out of the house, and roar once.

Frost-Bitten Vegetables

— Jin Yang

These days, the Old Zhengxing Restaurant must be serving stir-fried vegetable hearts! Whether stir-fried with sliced meat, stir-fried with dried shrimp... or even just simply stir-fried in oil, I think everyone will praise the long taste of this vegetable heart.

Vegetables only gradually become delicious after the Beginning of Winter because frost has begun to be blown down to the ground by the gusty cold wind. It enters the heart of the vegetable, it covers the leaves of the vegetable. Vegetables that have been frost-bitten are glutinous and sweet.

Frost is universally spread over everything on the ground. It beats the vegetables and also beats people!

Those night workers who can't go home until three or four in the morning every night; those men and women factory workers who walk in groups of three or five every day before the moon has set, or huddle in piles on single-wheeled carts, pushing and running from the slums hidden in another corner of the city to the chimneys of the factories, working harder than "working at sunrise"; they are all accustomed to being ravaged by wind and rain, and are "bitter" sufferers of frost and dew:

Their feelings are certainly not as sensitive as our poets, but they have not been completely numb, right? What kind of emotions should surge in each of their simple minds, in each of their weak hearts? In the late night of early winter when the wind is tight and the frost and dew are heavy! At the dawn of early winter!

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: Desiring to Leave and Desiring to Stay, Remembering Past Events in the Same Car; Half Crying and Half Smiling, Leaning on the Pillow, Sick in Late Autumn

When she got into the car, she thought that Ji Zhi was just an old neighbor, how could she shake hands with him in front of so many people? Fortunately, there wasn't a single acquaintance on the bus, otherwise, what would happen if this got back to Haidian? Her heart pounded at this thought. But how could Ji Zhi understand this reason? The seats in this bus were two long planks attached to the walls on both sides. People with tickets crowded onto the bus, and the seats were already so packed that there wasn't any space. Ji Zhi had prepared for this move, sitting diagonally, stretching out his legs, occupying some space on the bench. Gui Zhi stood in the middle of the car, at a loss. Ji Zhi quickly sat down, squeezing hard, and making a small space in the corner of the car. He patted it with his hand and said, "Sit down, sit down!" Gui Zhi had no choice standing there. When someone offered her a seat, how could she not sit down? She had to squeeze in and sit down. But just as she sat down, a thought immediately arose in her mind? Even when she and Ji Zhi were very close, they had never sat together like this. Now that she was a married woman, she was sitting so close to him, wasn't this an unexpected thing? Maybe he was deliberately setting a trap, she couldn't fall for it. But she was already sitting down, and there was no reason to stand up. Otherwise, for such a long journey, she would have a seat and not sit, standing in the car, wouldn't people say she was crazy? So she turned her body to the side, facing away from Ji Zhi. The car started, and the people on the car began to talk. In Ji Zhi's heart, he was thinking that he had never sat so close to Gui Zhi, shoulder to shoulder, in the days when they were closest. Now, she had a hidden fragrance of powder on her body, sending it to people's noses faintly. After smelling it, there was an inexplicable sense of pleasure (252)

Character Sketches

— Jin Zi

Lawyer Zheng's Wine

Wine is truly something enjoyed by both the refined and the vulgar, and it has traces since the beginning of history. If we look at the biographies of various countries, we can easily find many "wine" characters and many "drunk" characters that are most closely related to wine. After the Qin and Han dynasties, the power of wine expanded even more. People like Chun Yukun and Liu Ling became famous throughout the world for their ability to drink, and their names were passed down through the ages. Their exemplary virtues and reputations are still remembered by a group of drunkards. There were also those friends who could write, such as Li Taibai and Ouyang Xiu, who complemented each other because they could both write and drink good wine, enjoying great fame for thousands of years. However, they were indeed flattered by the wine and benefited a lot. But the wine also owes it to them for promoting it like this, immediately raising its value, so that the famous scholars of later generations knew that wine could be drunk and would not be prohibited by moralists. By the Republic of China, there were the elegant stories of Mr. Luo Wengan and Mr. Zheng Tianxi, both serving as Ministers of Justice, and both fond of Huadiao and Brandy.

I don't know how much Mr. Luo Wengan could drink, or how addicted he was to wine, so I dare not boast on his behalf. But I heard that Mr. Luo had eye disease last time, his eyes were all red. The doctor taught him not to drink wine again, but he only kept the fast for half a day, and in the evening, he still poured down large bowls and pots as usual. From this, we can see a glimpse of it. Now, let's get back to the main topic and talk about Mr. Zheng Tianxi alone. Mr. Zheng is a big fat man who used to be a lawyer in Shanghai. It is said that no matter how busy he was with legal affairs, he had to drink after six o'clock in the afternoon. He would no longer consult about anything, but just sip and sip slowly until he rested in the evening. But he had three admirable good habits about how he liked to drink: First, he never drank himself drunk; second, he would not drink foreign wine unless he had to; third, he never drank more than the fixed amount every day; because even though he spent time with wine every day, he never lost his temper.

Mr. Zheng had a very strong ability to distinguish wine. He knew whether it was good or bad as soon as he tasted it. Because he was a regular customer of Wang Baohe, he once obtained the permission of the owner to try each type of wine in their store. At the end of the tasting, Mr. Zheng pointed out that a certain wine was really a priceless treasure. The owner was overjoyed when he heard this. He said that Mr. Zheng was really a person who could drink wine and was worthy of drinking this kind of wine. From that day on, he informed the waiter that whenever Mr. Zheng went to drink, he was allowed to provide him with that special wine. At that time, Mr. Zheng was still working as a lawyer, so the owner and the waiter called that wine "Lawyer Zheng's Wine" to commemorate it.

Director Huang's Meal

Eating is the only big thing and the only common thing in life, what is so rare about it. But the eating of Mr. Huang Boqiao, the current director of the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau, is really not a normal thing, how can it not be recorded.

Director Huang suffered from diabetes several years ago, not only was he hopeless to have children, but he was also externally strong but internally weak, and he would lie down at any time. So he listened to the doctor's advice and implemented qualitative and quantitative eating. The so-called qualitative is to specify the nature of the food. What he stipulated were a few very simple types: The first was black bread (also known as bran bread) with a little butter; the second was yellow rice. The dishes emphasized liquids, and he didn't eat anything that was too fresh, nor did he eat anything that was too starchy, and he only ate a very few kinds. As for the quantitative, it was to specify the amount of bread and rice to be eaten. Therefore, whether he invited people to dinner himself or people invited him to dinner, all he needed was a basin of soup. When it was time to eat, he first said "please", and then took out two or three pieces of black bread that his wife had weighed and cut into pieces and wrapped in white paper from his pocket, and chewed them slowly. If he was at home, then what he ate would definitely be yellow rice that was also grown by his wife, and he probably wouldn't eat even one extra grain.

It is said that he has been implementing the above situation for five or six years, and although his diabetes has not been completely cured, his spirit is indeed better than before.

Student Unrest Erupts Again at Shandong First High School: Students Unite to Expel Sun Weiyue, Banners and Leaflets are Bizarre

(Jinan Correspondence) In recent years, education in this province has been straightened out, educational funding is never in arrears, and normal education, secondary education, vocational education, and rural education are all thriving. However, the provincial First High School has experienced repeated student unrest in the past two years, causing social criticism. Last year, the Department of Education, under orders, held the first entrance examination. Senior high school students and students of the school took the lead in opposing it. Principal Sun Weiyue was not good at handling it, which led to the expansion of the student unrest and even resulted in the absurd drama of beating the provincial supervisor Ma Rumei. Fortunately, the Department of Education decisively put down the unrest. For the past year, Sun has been derelict in his duties as before, and the head of the education department Hu Ganqing and the head of student affairs Wang Xintang have colluded with Sun, which has made the students even more dissatisfied. Thus, they brewed a student movement to expel Sun. Yesterday was Saturday, and due to a certain incident, the student unrest suddenly broke out. Numerous banners and leaflets were found throughout the school, with the words "Down with Sun Dongsheng (Sun Weiyue's nickname)", "Hu Ganqing", "Wang Xintang", and various bizarre terms such as "Expel the Bastard Sun Dongsheng". Some teachers left the school when they saw the sudden outbreak of student unrest. Therefore, yesterday passed hastily in a disorganized manner. It is not yet known whether classes will be held tomorrow, which is a holiday. It is faintly heard that the students are determined to expel Sun and will not stop until they achieve their goal.

Overview of the Chinese Institute of the University of Paris

Liu Hou, the Chinese government representative of the Chinese Institute of the University of Paris, recently reported the overview of the Chinese Institute of the University of Paris to the Chinese Ministry of Education. The original report is as follows:

(1) History In the autumn of the eighth year of the Republic of China, Mr. Wu Zhihui published a proposal for overseas emigration, advocating that the funds for establishing universities in the country should be transferred to establish universities overseas, so that the country's universities could create teachers in a better environment. Mr. Li Shizeng and Wang Jingwei were in France at the time and immediately agreed with his statement, which led to the establishment of the Sino-French Institute of the University of Lyon. At the same time, Mr. Ye Gongchuo was investigating in Europe and wanted to spread Oriental culture to France. He planned to have the Ministry of Communications fund the establishment of a Chinese Institute within the University of Paris, where Chinese academics would teach French people. Together with Mr. Han Rujia, he consulted Mr. Ban Lewei, the former Prime Minister of France, a scholar and statesman, on this idea. Mr. Ban strongly agreed and agreed to preside over the matter. On March 22, in the ninth year of the Republic of China, a society was established called the Chinese Institute. Its purposes were fivefold: (1) to help organize a mechanism for studying new and old advanced Chinese knowledge within the University of Paris, (1) to establish a Chinese library, and to train Chinese library specialists and translators, (3) to organize and encourage all Chinese-French institutions that can enable French people to study advanced Chinese knowledge, or Chinese people to study advanced French knowledge, (4) to assist in the establishment of the Chinese Academy of Sciences Academie Chinoise Des Sciences as a supplement to the old Chinese "Academy" and the preparation for the development of Western science in China, (5) to publish various publications, organize various special research associations and lectures, and issue prizes and subsidies. This society was recognized by the French government on December 12, in the tenth year of the Republic of China, and was affiliated with the University of Paris on March 17, in the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, and was named the Chinese Institute of the University of Paris. (To be continued)

China: Scout Specialist Qualification Training Standards (5)

(39) Horticulture 1. Able to independently cultivate a plot of land of three square meters or more; 2. Able to plant five kinds of melons, vegetables, or flowers and fruits and have results, and must make a report; 3. Able to recognize more than ten kinds of flowers and trees in the garden and know the general planting methods; 4. Know the methods of pruning, irrigation, fertilization, grafting, transplanting, etc.; 5. Able to make beautiful garden designs.

(40) Electricity 1. Know the basic knowledge of electricity; 2. Know the principles and functions of various simple batteries; 3. Able to make simple electromagnets; 4. Know the relationship between current, voltage, resistance, and wires; 5. Know the internal structure of electric bells and telephones and the flow of electricity; 6. Able to repair and connect wires and install electric lights, telephones, and electric bells; 7. Know first aid for electric shock.

(41) Telegraph 1. Able to understand various simple circuits; 2. Able to understand the structure of telegraph machines and simple repair methods; 3. Able to send and receive Chinese Morse code at a rate of ten characters per minute or more, or English Morse code at a rate of forty letters per minute or more; 4. Able to understand the general principles of wireless telegraph equipment.

(42) Cooking 1. Able to build various camp stoves; 2. Able to cook eight kinds of meat and vegetarian dishes; 3. Know the methods of smoking and grilling food and making summer refreshing drinks; 4. Able to make one kind of Chinese and Western pastry each; 5. Know the methods of preventing food spoilage and storage.

(43) Taxidermy Specimen Making 1. Know the methods of taxidermy, immersion, and drying of animal specimens; 2. Know the methods of collecting, making, and preserving insect specimens; 3. Know the methods of collecting and making plant specimens; 4. Know the tools and medicines used for taxidermy of animal specimens; 5. Able to make two kinds of animal specimens; 6. Able to collect ten kinds of insects and plants each and make them into specimens; 7. Able to collect five kinds of mineral, rock, or fossil specimens.

(44) Swimming 1. Able to swim fifty meters without removing clothes and shoes; 2. Able to remove clothes and shoes in the water; 3. Able to swim one hundred meters in three different styles; 4. Able to dive and find objects underwater; 5. Know rescue methods for drowning; 6. Able to play three or more kinds of games in the water.

(45) Hunting 1. Know the hunting seasons of the year and the method of identifying beneficial birds; 2. Be familiar with the habits of birds and animals; 3. Able to detect and track birds and animals by their footprints; 4. Able to shoot birds and animals in action; 5. Know various hunting methods; 6. Know the training methods of hunting dogs; 7. Know the use and protection of hunting guns.

Argentina Builds Great Sports Field to Prepare for World Games

Twelfth Session May Be Held in Argentina

(Reuters, Buenos Aires, November 27) Buenos Aires is preparing for the World Olympic Games to be held in Argentina in the future. After the government approves the Argentine currency of 6 million (equivalent to £470,000), the construction of the national sports field will begin immediately. This field can accommodate 100,000 seats and has large-scale track and field events and international football games. The law for the construction of the sports field was passed in 1921, but its final construction plan has only recently been approved. The track of the athletic field is half a mile.

The future World Olympic Games, or the twelfth session, may be held here if it is in Argentina.

Special Article: A General Overview of Modern Chinese Educational Thought (9) - Lecture by Shu Xincheng, Notes by Sun Yucai: Thoughts on Women's Education

Thoughts on women's education occupy a considerable position in the entire history of educational thought. Currently, we can only temporarily discuss several names related to its evolution. Detailed information requires consulting specialized works. These include: the "Good Mother, Wise Wife" educational ideology, the female national education ideology, gender equality education, and women's education. Although there have been many variations in the thoughts on women's education over the past thirty years, they can be broadly divided into the four main strands mentioned above. The emergence of these four ideologies is not accidental; they share common causes and specific backgrounds. The former arises from changes in social organization, while the latter is driven by the agitation of family values, national ideologies, human rights principles, and scientific thought. However, for women's education to develop in the same way as men's education, it is still necessary to adhere to the scientific principles of women's education and make special efforts.

New Paths in Education Going Forward

To determine the direction of Chinese educational thought going forward, first, it must be understood that education is a part of human activity and cannot be separated from other activities. The ideals and realities of society, politics, and economics all play a role in governing education. Therefore, the reform of education is not simply an educational problem but involves social, political, and economic factors. Although we are focusing on studying educational problems here, we must not hold preconceived notions and assume that education is all-powerful or ineffective. What we should pay attention to is the fact that education is a part of human activity. While it cannot be separated from other activities, its reform also affects those other activities. Therefore, to indicate future paths for education, we should clearly understand the situation in society, politics, and economics and establish a clear path to achieve our goals. Secondly, China's current situation is very special. Global trends are pushing it towards an industrial and commercial system from all sides, but its old organizational structures are hindering its progress due to transportation obstacles and the rampant presence of soldiers and bandits. In this transitional period, neither the old nor the new can be fully adopted; a new path must be developed by considering both.

Currently, China's politics are not on track, society is plagued by soldiers and bandits, lacking order and organization, and the economy is on the verge of bankruptcy. The phenomenon of a divided social life remains unchanged. There are two main reasons why China has reached this point: first, the oppression of the great powers; second, the population has been poisoned by the Confucian political thought of "not holding a position, not planning its policies" regarding national affairs.

Since the "September 18th Incident," the so-called justice and peace in the international community have been shown to be untrustworthy. Since the Lausanne Conference and the disarmament conference yielded no results, it has become clear that the so-called great powers have no economic way out, and war is inevitable. The success of the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan has also reminded us of the greatness of economy and popular intelligence in building a nation. In the future, if we want the Republic of China to stand independently in the world and the Chinese nation to exist forever on the earth, we must work hard to strengthen ourselves and build our country. In the process of self-strengthening and construction, education will naturally show its importance as a tool.

Now that we understand the crux of China's problems, what are the new paths for education going forward? There are several, which I have already mentioned: 1. Production education; 2. Rural education; 3. Popular education; 4. National rejuvenation education.

We deeply hope that our colleagues in the education field will work hard on production education, rural education, popular education, and national rejuvenation education. We also hope that educators will pay attention to politics, economics, and society outside of education to achieve coordination in education and jointly shoulder the responsibility of building the nation and the home, and revitalizing the nation. (End)

Free Talk

Literary Life and Slavery

— Tang Tao

From the beginning, making a living through writing has always been difficult. That's why when Barton (Bernad Barton) wanted to leave his bank job to devote himself to writing, Lamb (Charles Lamb) wrote to discourage him, telling him to sit safely in his bank office. The letter said something like this:

"If you rely on booksellers, squeezing your brains to exchange for a pot of ale and a few pieces of mutton, turning your free thoughts and lingering verses into commercial work, it's simply a slave's life, worse than any slave's life."

"Keep your bank; the bank will sustain you. Don't pay attention to worldly people. If you insist on the kind of status that gentlemen are concerned about, you will inevitably hang yourself, starve to death, or drown yourself."

Lamb first spoke of the hardships of a literary life, not as noble and leisurely as one might imagine. And trying to make a living this way always feels unreliable, so there's no need to give up your life to pursue the kind of status that worldly people are so concerned about. Although he said that a literary life is as difficult as slavery, it's not really slavery.

Chinese people hanging out signs to sell articles were rare in the past. But making a living by writing has "long been the case." To pass the imperial examination, become a successful candidate, and win the red and blue official hats, one had to be able to write a wonderful article "praising the sage's virtues" that would make the emperor "delighted." Then the wonderful article would be circulated, a good official position would be obtained, and the problem of livelihood would be solved.

In this way, the history of Chinese literature, as Mr. Yu Dafu said, has become a complete "history of slavery."

I'm afraid this kind of slavery is real, but it doesn't matter much. Because slavery in China is not as hateful as it is in foreign countries. China doesn't seem to have many Lambs. Traditional ideas tell us that being a slave with status is glorious and enjoyable; the problem is not about life. So if you try to stop others, you will inevitably offend them.

In recent times, signs for selling articles have been erected one after another. Life must still be lived, and we cannot persuade every writer to become an amateur, so writing articles and receiving royalties has been clearly stipulated and should not be "pursued." But the problem is naturally about life. If it's about enjoyment, glory, getting rich, being a slave with status, etc., outside of life, that's not covered by this rule.

But the ancient method should not be abolished after all. Slavery with status is "admired by all the world."

Peking Opera Connoisseur

— Sheng Fu

I don't often watch Peking Opera, but I'm not a follower of Mr. Liang Shuming, believing that I would feel uneasy inside if I saw Mei Lanfang once. Of course, it's not that I have a deeper understanding of art and look down on Peking Opera, so I don't want to go to the theater. The reason I don't often watch opera is that I don't have the leisure and lack the talent to be a Peking Opera connoisseur.

I admire Peking Opera connoisseurs very much. It is said that they can be roughly divided into three types:

One type cannot really be considered a "connoisseur." It refers to fools like me, who don't usually go to the theater. But when I occasionally visit, I'm a "play reader" in front of the stage, very concerned about the excitement on the stage. Who is playing Zhuge? What is her or his situation? And what kind of talented men and beauties are in the boxes? I don't even realize it, just watching the opera stupidly, one scene after another, and that's it.

Another type is a more profound connoisseur. Although they also sit in front of the stage, they rarely focus their eyes on the stage. We only see their activities: going up to the boxes for a while, going backstage for a while. They are busy enjoying "chewing gum" and "ice cream," and may even be holding a small publication. In short, they are busy and active, seemingly not watching the opera. However, they are more profound than you dull "readers." They can not only recite the plot and play the characters in the play, but also know all the secrets and private affairs of her or him; even those things that should not be told to others. Why are they so profound? Because they pay attention to the backstage, the actors, not the "play." They know that the "play" is not real, but just singing to deceive people to laugh and cry. After all, he is one level higher, and can doubly be called a connoisseur.

There is another type that I have only encountered in Beiping. These are connoisseurs who have entered samadhi. Their age is probably all "knowing destiny." They have thirty or forty years of connoisseurship history. Sometimes they have also acted in operas and taught students. Therefore, when they come to the theater, they simply don't need their eyes. We only see them sitting in the distant side boxes, closing their eyes and drinking "fragrant tea," sending their souls to another world with the curling sounds of the strings. They have truly entered samadhi. Of course, they don't go backstage or pay attention to the faces on the stage, but the theater boss never dares to offend them, because they have the authority to criticize. The words they say cannot be denied.

It is said that after Beijing was changed to Beiping, the market was sluggish. Recently, it was rumored that a new group of people in the Peking Opera troupes of Beiping went to the south to organize a stage, actively recruiting former famous actors and recruiting new younger generations, preparing to revive the past glory of Beijing Peking Opera. It is also said that the audience doesn't like to watch "The Substitute Prince," so this stage is preparing to stage some plays that suit the public's taste. In recent days, people who love Peking Opera in various places can't help but be a little moved, because the rumored repertoire is really too novel, and the distance from the old tunes is too far. I am a person with no connection to Peking Opera, and I don't want to criticize this new repertoire. I'm just wondering and worrying whether these famous actors who are famous for "The Substitute Prince" will still show the tail of the raccoon cat in this new play.

On Li Houzhu

— Yin Chuan

Anecdotes and stories about Li Yu, the Later Lord of Tang, are scattered in various records. If one puts in some effort to collect them, one can discover many important historical materials about him. From what I have seen and remember, in Kong Pingzhong's "Tan Yuan" of the Song Dynasty, it is recorded that Han Weigong had a painting of bamboo by Li Houzhu in his collection, saying that there were many inscriptions on it. Chen Meigong's "Pearl Boat" of the Ming Dynasty said, "Li Houzhu paid attention to writing instruments. The Chengxintang paper, Li Tinggui ink, and Longwei inkstone he used were the best in the world." Lu Youren's "Yanbei Magazine" said, "Yuan Bochang had a jade brush holder used by Li Houzhu, with engraved characters on it, the engraving being extremely fine." And another record in "Pearl Boat" simply mythologizes his anecdotes. The original record says:

Li Houzhu obtained a green stone inkstone. In the ink pool, there was a yellow stone like a pellet, the water was always full, and it was used all day without being depleted, and he always carried it with him. Later, when he returned to the court, Tao Gu saw it and was surprised. The inkstone was too big to hold, so he took the stone pellet away. Li Houzhu grabbed his hand and swung his arm onto the horse. Li Houzhu asked to thank him with treasures, but Tao refused. Li Houzhu said, "Only this inkstone can produce water, other inkstones cannot be used." Tao tried dozens of inkstones, but none produced water. Li Houzhu asked for it back very bitterly, but Tao could not bear to part with it and said, "I will have to break it." When the stone broke, a small fish jumped out of the ground and died. Since then, the inkstone has never been moist again.

These are all sufficient to help us understand Li Houzhu's life situation, although they cannot be said to be important materials. However, a note recorded in Yuan Qi of the Song Dynasty's "Maple Window Small Records" is extremely valuable, and it is a record of Li Houzhu's inscription. It is very difficult to find Li Houzhu's prose, and to suddenly obtain this article is like finding a treasure. The original record says:

I once saw a book in the inner library, "Jin Lou Zi," with a handwritten inscription by Li Houzhu saying, "Emperor Xiaoyuan of Liang said of Wang Zhongxuan, 'When I was in Jingzhou, I wrote dozens of books. When Jingzhou was destroyed, all the books were burned. Now there is one book left, which famous scholars all value. Seeing a hair of a tiger, one does not know its spots.' Later, when Western Wei broke Jiangling, the emperor also burned all the books, saying, 'The way of literature and martial arts ends tonight!' Why are the two phrases 'Jingzhou was destroyed and the books were burned' the same before and after?" He sighed in poetry: "Tens of thousands of axes of ivory tags are inside the red silk, Wang Can's books are also sent to the fire. If it were not for Emperor Zu Long leaving a face, how could the surviving chapters reach today?" The scrolls were all copied on Xue Tao paper, but "today" was mistakenly written as "Jin Dynasty." Emperor Huizong disliked it and erased it with a pen. Later, the book became a prophecy and entered the Jin Dynasty.

Li Houzhu's poetry and prose are all seen in this short note, and the fact that "today" was mistakenly written as "Jin Dynasty" can be said to be extremely clever. In "Yanbei Magazine," there are not only records about Li Houzhu, but also about Emperor Zhongzhu's portrait. One says that Li Boshi had a picture of Yadi, and Wang Mingqing determined that the person sitting upright was the portrait of Li Zhongzhu of the Southern Tang Dynasty. Another says, "Li Zhongzhu of Jiangnan, four brothers playing chess, the screen is written with Le Tian's poems, the colored figures on the paper are all lifelike." This painting is also related to Li Houzhu. Now I don't know where this painting has gone, or whether it is still in the world. Because I am recording Li Houzhu, I am also mentioning it.

Poor Child

— Xu Zhuanpeng

The mother had just coaxed her sick little brother to sleep when the seven-year-old child, who had been playing at the threshing ground early in the morning, came home flushed.

He stuck out his small, round, brown-blue eyes and said to his mother in a high-pitched voice:

"Mom, the beggar with the bamboo centipede is here again."

"Oh, that bewitching fellow. He'll kidnap children. Quickly close the door and hide in the corner..."

The mother put on a serious face and threatened him like this. She knew that when the child saw the beggar, he would want to buy his bamboo centipede and that would cost money.

The seven-year-old child already understood some things. He saw that all his companions liked the beggar and were happy when they saw him. They followed behind him, from street to street, from this alley to that alley, as if they didn't want to let him go... The beggar always smiled when he saw the children.

"Mom, you're lying to me. I want to buy a centipede to play with..." The child grabbed his mother's trouser leg and spun around her feet. He rolled around on the chicken-droppings-covered ground, trying to force his mother to give in by crying.

"I'll buy it next time. Mom doesn't have any money today."

The mother's gentle words were ineffective. The child's crying face would not turn into a smiling face until he got the centipede.

"Little Sanzi and Fifth Brother, they all bought one..."

"They are children from wealthy families. You can't compare to them... May you be reborn into a wealthy family in the next life..."

The seven-year-old child didn't understand his family's poverty, not even two copper coins to buy a box of matches! He only saw that his companions wanted one, so he wanted one too.

The beggar followed the children's cries, and at this moment, he was standing in front of her house.

"Buy one for the child to play with. Five copper coins is a small matter; it's a big deal if the child cries and hurts himself..."

Mothers with children all hated him, like a devil. When he came to the village, the children cried especially loudly.

"Go, go! No one wants to buy your centipede. Don't walk to my door. Next time, you're not allowed to come into our village..."

Even a storm of abuse couldn't drive him away. He still stood there, wanting to sell his wares.

The child saw that he couldn't get what he wanted and cried even more willfully.

"Okay, beggar, then I'll buy one from you. I don't have any money today. I'll bring it next time..."

"Hey! You want to owe the beggar money? Beggars who sell centipedes don't give credit..."

Then the beggar cast a contemptuous glance, spat on the ground, and walked to another house.

The mother, feeling wronged, vented her anger by hitting the child. At this moment, the mother wanted to use hitting to stop the child from crying.

"I wouldn't feel bad if I beat you to death, you little bastard... We don't even have enough to eat, where would we get the extra money to buy a centipede to play with..."

That day, the children in the village cried especially loudly, and many mothers beat their children...

Two Brothers (43)

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

Then he slowly reviewed all the conjectures that had made his heart ache last night on the embankment, amidst the sounds of the steam whistle. The more he thought about it, the more he felt that this matter was beyond doubt. He felt that he was being led by his own logic to that unpleasant fact, just like being led by a hand that dragged and strangled him.

He was thirsty, he was hot. His heart was pounding.

He stood up to open the window to breathe, but as he stood up, a slight sound came from the wall next door.

Jean was sleeping peacefully and snoring softly. He was sleeping, him! He had not anticipated anything, had not guessed anything! A man who knew their mother left all his property to him. He took the money, feeling that this was righteous and natural.

He was sleeping, rich and satisfied, but he didn't know that his brother was in torment. So Pierre felt a surge of anger towards this carefree, satisfied sleeper.

If it had been last night, he would have gone to knock on his door, walked in, and sat in front of his bed. He would have said to him, suddenly waking up and surprised, "Jean, you shouldn't accept this inheritance. It will make others suspect our mother and thus damage her reputation."

But today he could no longer speak. He couldn't tell Jean that he absolutely didn't believe he was their father's son. Now he had to keep this shameful discovery to himself, keep the secret in his heart. He had to hide the stain he had seen so that no one would notice, not even his brother, especially his brother.

He no longer thought about the irrelevant praise or slander of public opinion. He would rather everyone slander his mother, as long as he knew she was innocent, as long as he alone knew. How could he live with her every day, looking at her while thinking that she had conceived his brother under the caresses of a stranger? How could he endure this?

But how peaceful and cheerful she was, how innocent she seemed! Could a woman like her, a woman with a pure soul and a righteous heart, fall, be seduced by passion, and then not show any remorse, not show that she had ever been troubled by her conscience?

Yarn and Cloth: Yarn Prices Could Not Be Maintained · Yesterday's Market Price Fell Sharply · Turning to Self-Preservation Amidst Irreversible Torrent

Therefore, there is no expectation of further declines in the future. However, Hanjiang tung oil remains weak. If not, it is possible to abandon the south and go for the north. Therefore, each transaction is not for a large amount, also restricted by the Hankou market.

Conversations

Observing Various Things

— Lizhai

Inventing brand new terms and jargon is clearly one of the specialties of our Eastern neighbor, the "friendly nation." When panic strikes, the "friendly nation" calls it "economic recession." When Hoover deferred debt payments, they called it "Hoover recovery." When Uchida came to power, we had the opportunity to learn about "scorched earth diplomacy." When Hirota took office, we were again learning about "rational diplomacy." In addition, the most clamorous in recent "dwarfed writing" newspapers is "quiet observation" of various things. Adopting "quiet observationism" towards the "anti-foreign movement in China," they now want to "quietly observe" the future development of the resumption of diplomatic relations between the US and Russia.

Regarding "quiet observation" of various things, it is not only not lacking among "domestic products," but also among "domestic people," there is no shortage of those who have "reached the pinnacle." Therefore, if one envies and sighs at the "quiet observation" of the "friendly nation," then one is either unfamiliar with "national studies" or a "fool" of the "big melon" world!

In Chinese stories and idioms, such as "Bian Zhuang stabbing the tiger" and "the snipe and clam fighting, the fisherman benefits," all have "quiet observationism" as their core. And like "think thrice before acting," it also has a very strong "meaning of quiet observation." Those who "think thrice" must ensure that there is no danger "before," no hidden trouble "after," and that the "present" has benefits that can be obtained without owing anything. Without "quietly" "observing," how can this painstaking effort be achieved?

As for "straddling two boats" and "watching the wind to steer the rudder," they are even more timeless "classics" of "quiet observationism," and "domestic" "politicians" or "traders," especially those who can be called "consummate skills" in this way!

"Quiet observationism" is always advantageous for individuals. Some "revolutionary leaders" or "philanthropists" who have made great fortunes are well-deserved, all obtained from "quiet observation." However, this kind of "benefiting the world before benefiting oneself" "quiet observation" is often more ominous than auspicious for the national nation. Therefore, there were too many "quiet observation" gentlemen in the two Jin dynasties, resulting in the invitation of Wang Hu's alien races to create more than a hundred years of dark history for China. The "quiet observation" gentlemen of the Southern Song Dynasty had not yet reached a conclusion, and the Jin soldiers had already crossed the river. And now, the quantity and quality of "quiet observationists" in China is an unprecedented spectacle, so where will our national nation go? This does not require looking at anything else, just looking at the foreign flags fluttering at the mouths of the Great Wall and some of the first- and second-class dignitaries busily purchasing villas and property in the "British" or "French" concessions in Shanghai, one can vaguely imagine its future.

Under the Wheels

— Yüsheng

Winter days are especially short, and it's dark before six o'clock. This evening, it's drizzling again, so this quiet road seems especially desolate!

"Woo! Woo!" A yarn factory beside the road is sounding the return echo. The two interrupted sounds indicate the 9:45 signal that the shift is about to change.

In less than a quarter of an hour, this dead road came back to life, especially at the entrance of the yarn factory. Peddlers carrying baskets and shouting; the idle "road heroes" lingering around; the family members of workers waiting for work to end with their oil shoes and umbrellas: and the endless stream of male and female workers going to the night shift, almost blocking this short stretch of road.

The clock on the yarn factory building moved forward minute by minute, and the active and noisy crowd became even more chaotic with the passage of time.

"Woo!" A car came speeding from afar.

"Bang!" When it broke into the center of the crowd, there was a sudden loud noise, and every face immediately showed tension, and they were using their ears and eyes to find out what had happened.

"Mom... Save... Me!" An unusual, tragic, and mournful sound wave broke the momentary silence.

"A car has run someone over!" Someone was shouting loudly.

The crowd immediately boiled over and flocked together like dark clouds covering the sky, quickly surrounding the car.

The engine had not yet stopped, and the driver wanted to step on the gas and escape.

"Bang!" The front window of the car had already been broken by a large worker.

"Damn it! Stop, do you still want to run?" Several people shouted in unison.

"Hit!" "Hit!" The crowd shouted wildly.

"Bang!" "Bang!" "Bang!" Three more windows on the car were broken in succession.

"Agen! Stop the car!" The gentleman sitting in the back of the car commanded his driver.

"Ah! Save... Me!" The already hoarse voice came from under the car.

"Someone is dying, quickly drag them out to see!" The eldest son, who was standing at the front, reminded everyone with a smart word, and three or four good men immediately emerged from the crowd, rolling up their sleeves and beginning to drag.

"Ouch!..." An extremely painful cry.

"The wheel has crushed the left arm, the car should be moved backward."

The driver slowly backed the car about five inches.

"Good!" Amidst everyone's approval, a young girl of seventeen or eighteen was dragged out of the wheel seam. The dirt on the road and fresh red blood covered his clothes, hair, and face. He was breathing rapidly with weak groans, still bleeding at the corners of his mouth, and his left arm was hanging limp behind his back.

"Damn it! You pigs in the car! Why don't you get out!" A sharp scream from the crowd.

The car door opened, and a short and fat gentleman came out of the car, wearing a very elegant Western suit, covered with a full-wool tweed coat, with a pair of cunning faces wearing glasses. He looked very embarrassed, but deliberately pretended to be very calm.

"Are you alright! It didn't crush you, did it!" The gentleman's tone was somewhat contrived, and the sound waves trembled slightly.

"Damn it! People are dying! And you say it didn't crush you!" The big man cursed angrily.

"Slap!" The gentleman's right face had already been slapped, half of it as red as pig's blood.

"Let's be civilized! Anyway, I'll take responsibility!" The gentleman surrendered.

"Ping!" He was hit twice in the waist again, this was done by a short man, his fists still clenched and unwilling to relax, as if he still needed to "continue to work hard".

"Everyone, don't fight! It's important to save people first!" The intelligent eldest son was most concerned about the person who had been crushed, and a word reminded everyone, so everyone's eyes shifted back to the unfortunate girl, releasing the gentleman from the siege.

"Yes! Send them to the hospital immediately, take my car, Agen! Come down and help him into the car." The gentleman, who was best at watching the wind, had received a pardon, but he still maintained the dignity of the owner when giving orders to the driver.

The driver, Agen, who was hiding in the corner of the front compartment of the car, was awakened from his nightmare by his master. He held the little girl's waist in both hands and pushed her forward.

"No! Where's my lunch box?" The poor little girl, when he was about to die, still remembered his life – the lunch box!

"Oh! Really, let's help him find it!" The eldest son was giving orders. After a few minutes of confusion, a lead lunch box was found in a small ditch two or three zhang away from the car. The originally rectangular box had turned hexagonal. The rice was spilled, and it was quickly passed from outside the crowd to the little girl's front in a "pass" manner. He was helped into the back seat by the driver and three or four workers. The snow-white cushion was covered with mud and blood.

Mr. Ba Shuhai, named Chengzhi, from She County, Anhui Province

"Woo!" The crowd split apart like a volcanic eruption, and the car carefully passed through the crack, like a criminal about to be executed escaping from the execution ground, speeding forward, and finally disappeared under the splashing mud and dim lights.

Controlled Economy and Planned Economy

— Su

The term "controlled economy" has been frequently heard in the mouths of Chinese intellectuals recently. They all feel that in today's bankrupt rural economy, the rural area cannot be revived without implementing a controlled economy. Therefore, the central government has established an economic committee, which is related to various control committees, so that all production can have a proper supply under various controls.

The so-called planned economy appeared at the same time as the controlled economy. Some people say that this is the controlled economy, while others say that this is a part of the controlled economy. Both are wrong. The following explains them separately:

Both controlled economy and planned economy are types of economic policies, but their contents are very different. A controlled economy does not have a specific plan, and only corrects the economic condition when it becomes morbid, such as increasing production when there is insufficient production, and decreasing production when there is too much. However, a planned economy has a specific plan, and all economic activities are carried out according to a certain plan. It focuses on production, engaging in a large amount of production.

Furthermore, countries that implement a controlled economy recognize the existence of private property, but only impose appropriate restrictions. However, countries that implement a planned economy never allow private property, because private property hinders the implementation of a planned economy.

From the above, it can be known that a controlled economy pays attention to consumption, while a planned economy pays attention to production. The former takes care of the present, while the latter plans for the future. Although the forms of the two seem different, the ultimate goal is to maintain a balance between production and consumption, so that there is no excessive surplus or shortage.

Amateur Mailbox: Divorce is Never a Matter Worth Promoting

Editor

My good friend, a year ago, married a man she had never met before by the order of her parents and the words of a matchmaker. Before marriage, she worked at a certain bank, and always harbored the ambition of independence; but she was unfortunately born in an old-fashioned and corrupt family, which thought that when a woman grows up, she should marry. When she was only eighteen years old, she had no choice but to enter a complicated family under the authority of her parents. Not long after the marriage, her mother-in-law died; although there were no elders above her, she had many sisters and brothers. Their feelings also deteriorated day by day due to different opinions. Although they have only been married for a year, both parties have decided to separate, and the other party is willing to pay her alimony. However, her mother's family is an old family, and they are not old enough to be independent. I request

Editor to reply to Shi Peizhen.

Editor's note: Divorce is never a matter worth promoting. A married couple who separates in the middle of their lives, not to mention the suffering of those who have children, even those who do not have children suffer deep and intense mental trauma. For the sake of enabling them to enjoy comparative happiness, we cannot but allow consensual divorce for couples who are unhappy. However, this kind of event is like a person developing a malignant sore, and it is imperative to apply a knife; but for the patient's vitality, it is harmful after all. We should be social pathologists, exploring the causes of these unhappy couples, and shouting loudly to warn society, so that this unfortunate event can disappear into nothingness.

Miss Shi's friend's relationship with her husband has already broken down, like a malignant sore that has already formed. Direct separation is the right thing to do. As for the stubbornness of her parents, it is not a problem. According to the stubborn argument, the first marriage of a woman should be decided by her parents, and the second marriage can be decided by herself; at most, she will not get help from her parents in the future. As for the fact that she is not yet an adult, the law stipulates that married men and women, regardless of whether they are adults or not, are deemed to have the ability to act, so there is no need to worry. However, those who are too young are prone to being deceived; if this mistake is a big one, they can still blame their parents, but if there are any mistakes in the future, they are no one to blame. If they do not divorce, it will be difficult to live day by day, and if they do, the future is bleak in the vast sea of ​​people. Therefore, they have to rely on their best friends to help them at any time.

In our opinion, the reason why the relationship between the couple has broken down so badly is complex, but the most important point is probably the "extended family system." It is inevitable that a woman who is usually highly valued will have horizontal opinions when she is in the midst of many uncles, aunts, cousins, and aunts. We propose that the lady and others may as well try to form a small family separately. Once the root of the opinion is cut off, the qin and se may be readjusted. If it does not work, it is not too late to divorce. I wonder how likely this suggestion is to be realized?

She is now willing to work as a typist or other clerk in any institution. If there is a need for this talent, please reply to the Amateur Weekly of this newspaper.

Mr. Shen, from Jiaxing, Zhejiang, 25 years old, graduated from the Department of Electrical Engineering of National Jiaotong University, and is proficient in English and German. He is willing to work as a radio engineer in public or private institutions. He can also teach part-time at night. Those who want to hire him, please contact Mr. Chen of the Nanyang Alumni Association on the 5th floor of the Mainland Shopping Mall. Feng Yangwu, from Shanghai, 24 years old, graduated from high school, has worked as an elementary school teacher, newspaper editor, and proofreader, and has some research on new literature. He is now willing to take on the above positions, regardless of monthly salary, but must provide board and lodging. If you want to hire him, please send a letter to the Huizhong Hotel, Shandong Road.

Fiction

Shanghai (6)

— Zhang Laosan

(11) City Girls

Across from me was a group of typical Shanghai girls. Listening to their nonsensical chatter, it was as if they were also going to the preaching conference. It probably felt like attending a national goods exhibition, wearing a few homespun cheongsams, and basking in the compliments of socialites and "queens." Maybe they were even going to dabble in vegetarianism and scripture chanting.

They were all dressed alike, in a kind of gray silk fabric. Their thin lined jackets were nowhere near as thick as our old cloth robes, with short sleeves and stiff collars. A friend of mine once said bluntly, "Shanghai girls, as long as it's fashionable, they'll do anything. If some big shot sponsored a modeling contest, they'd strip off their pants and rush to join."

Little Huang said these words after a heartbreak. His friends laughed at him for being too cowardly, but I sympathized with him, thinking there was some truth in his words. Because of this thought, I glanced at them a few more times. They seemed to notice me too. They began to whisper among themselves. I was aware that my old cloth cotton robe was out of place in this carriage. Even if I couldn't afford a stiff Western suit, I should at least have a long robe with a stiff collar and a narrow waist. However, it was also partly my fault for daring to glance at them too much. Stealing a glance out the window, I saw that Xujiahui was approaching, so I ignored their snickers, reopened my newspaper, and avoided their gaze.

Today, Xujiahui was like the incense fair at Jing'an Temple, with cars arriving one after another. Stepping off the tram, even more surprisingly, a swarm of rickshaws surrounded me. I pushed my way out of the crowd and headed towards the "extraterritorial villa." That group of city girls suddenly saved a few coppers on rickshaw fare, using their beautiful but unhealthy legs, accustomed to riding in cars. They followed behind me, chattering and giggling, clearly making this country bumpkin the center of their conversation. You probably think I'm respectfully attending the preaching conference of the great philanthropist Xu Bingnan. I know I'm an unfashionable person, but even for Shanghai's so-called "modern" preaching conferences, I shouldn't belong there. You're judging a country bumpkin by your modern minds, which is too much of an insult to me. I turned around and glared at them angrily. They burst out laughing even louder. City girls! Go play with the young masters who follow under your fashionable cheongsams every day. Making fun of a country bumpkin like me, your victory isn't worth a laugh!

(12) Pingdi, it's you!

The first guests to enter the extraterritorial villa with their heads held high all had a special badge as a talisman. I was mixed in with the crowd when the doorman stopped me. He looked me up and down with disdain, his triangular eyes scanning my clothing.

"What do you want?" The proprietary tone of a superior to a subordinate.

"Can I see Mr. Xu Bingnan?"

I knew that even the King of Hell was easier to see than his underlings, so I asked politely.

"He's not receiving guests today!"

I wanted to explain that Xu Bingnan was my uncle, but looking at my old cloth cotton robe, no one would believe that the great philanthropist Xu Bingnan had such a low-class nephew. So I handed over my business card and said humbly,

"Please trouble you to present my card."

Unexpectedly, the laughter I had heard before came from behind again. That group of girls was standing behind me, and the leader clapped her hands, jumped forward, and shouted,

"Pingdi, it's you!"

I was stunned for a moment. The doorman was already standing like a wooden figure in a shop window, trembling and saying, "Miss, you're back." Only then did I realize it was my cousin Xu Huiqin, who cried all day because I accidentally broke her goldfish bowl. She turned back to the group of girls and said,

"I didn't recognize him wrongly!" She laughed again like she'd won a gamble. "You wait in the front hall, I'll take Pingdi to see Papa."

"Miss, the master is in the second concubine's room."

The doorman looked at me pitifully. He didn't expect a country bumpkin in a cotton robe to be the young lady's brother. He eagerly said that the master was in the second concubine's room, partly to please the young lady and partly hoping that I wouldn't say anything about his slow treatment in front of the master. We unfashionable young people can find examples everywhere of bumping into the nails of the "second masters." Seeing their attitude of looking down on us, I hated myself for studying so many years, not even having the prestige of a "second master." But seeing their groveling faces, I felt sorry for their circumstances. I gave him a kind look. My cousin didn't understand his meaning and glared at him angrily, "I know!"

Later, I learned that my cousin was dissatisfied with each of the concubines.
