Film Special

Interview with Chinese Film Artists (23) Continued from November 14th

— Sha Ji

(10) Cai Chusheng, Director of "Morning of the Metropolis" (Part 1)

This is another very promising young filmmaker. He's only twenty-seven this year. In foreign literature, people of his age are often called "endearingly strange children." But in "Morning of the Metropolis," he already has remarkable achievements.

I don't think this is just temporary praise. Everyone must admit that he has artistic genius in his works. And I'm not just a "corner-boosting" Zhou Lang. Why would I want to praise someone? In ancient times, many young people had overly high expectations for generals, waiting anxiously for them to come to power and govern the country, so they enthusiastically supported them. Who knew that after the generals came to power, they would transform into fierce, blue-faced demons, launching a great slaughter. Those who had previously supported them were chopped into mincemeat under the butcher's knife. Thinking back on those events, I still feel frightened. How dare I support anyone?

Enough digression. I was walking along the gloomy Yanping Road one evening and approached the Lianhua Second Factory's studio. In the corridor on the second floor, I saw Yuan Congmei, famous for playing villainous roles, wearing a rather beautiful evening dress, her face like jade and her lips like vermilion. Shang Guanwu was also tidying up the newly glued-on mustache in front of the mirror. Understanding dawned on me. I knew they were getting dressed up to appear on the screen again.

Soon, Mr. Cai came up from downstairs. I said "Hello," and he also said "Hello," so we went into the director's office together. There, I saw Tan Ying, whom I had learned from twice in "Such a Hero" and "The Street Cleaner," writing a letter, rustling the paper. However, I didn't dare to bother her too much. In all conscience, I simply asked:

"Ms. Tan Ying, what plays have you been in recently?"

"Wind," he said. "Directed by Mr. Wu Cun..." I couldn't hear the rest clearly. I had to just nod along. In fact, it was already quite presumptuous to be so forward with a female star. As for the gentlemen who consider female stars "lovers of the masses," that's a different story altogether.

Soon, Director Cai took out a pack of chewing gum from his coat pocket. I chewed a piece, soft and sweet. I heard him say:

"Alright, now that we have tea, cigarettes, and candy, we can start talking."

"I think you should just talk freely," I said.

"But what should I say?" he said. "In these turbulent years, it's really not easy to speak. I've wanted to write something for your newspaper several times, but due to various reasons, I had to keep my mouth shut like a golden man. That's one aspect. On the other hand, when movies were still in the hands of the 'Mandarin Ducks and Butterflies School,' I dared to write a little something. But now that many progressive writers are paying attention to movies, I don't dare to write anything. I haven't read enough, I'm shallow, and I don't understand theory. If I were to write something, wouldn't it be like showing off in front of a master carpenter? So I think it's better for readers to get to know me through my works."

Dear readers, you see how modest he is. Unable to resist my urging, he finally spoke at length.

"Chinese cinema has finally had a history of one or two decades, but does it fulfill its proper mission now? That's still a big question. On the one hand, it's certainly due to economic constraints, but that dangerous severity has slowly disappeared. So what's most needed now is sound talent.

"Speaking of film talent, that's really not easy to cultivate. For example, to be a director, you need knowledge in all aspects. Cinema is a comprehensive art, encompassing literature, drama, painting, sculpture, architecture, music, and even human relationships and understanding of society. You need deep cultivation and understanding. But if you examine the Chinese film talent, you can say that since its history, there has never been a complete one. At the same time, the motivations for people to engage in film are also very complex. Some come with bad intentions. Because of this, for Chinese cinema to embark on a sound path, it is at least not possible at present. (To be continued)

Film Review "Rose Villa"

— Ping Moer

"At The Villa Rose"

The social basis of detective films is the same as that of martial arts films. We don't need to say much. We only need to ask who the so-called "detective" serves to know!

Because of the widespread sales of the popular novel "Sherlock Holmes," the whole world knows about the detective skills of England. Therefore, we naturally have some hope for the British detective film "Rose Villa" in terms of plot.

But this hope was finally shattered. The strength of detective films naturally lies in "red herrings," in other words, the bizarreness of the plot. However, no matter how many "red herrings" and how bizarre, the audience will always gradually understand the result. But this "Rose Villa" is not like that at all. The last section of the film simply narrates the second half of the film:

"...the ending is particularly unexpected. Who the murderer is remains a mystery until the very last moment." Naturally, using a method like "Rose Villa" can make the audience feel especially strange. But the audience's feeling must be that it's too strange, because there is not a single clue to be found in the middle.

It is most difficult for the director to handle detective films, because if the story is presented clearly, the audience feels it is ordinary; if the story is made too bizarre, the audience feels it is strange and unreasonable. Therefore, the director of a detective film should first have an extremely precise scientific mind, and secondly, should be rich in suggestive techniques. Because this can prevent the film from becoming overly idealized, and at the same time can prevent the film from becoming ordinary. The director of "Rose Villa" has not achieved these two points.

Originally, detective films must first be reasonable. Their ability to make people feel interested because of surprise is entirely because there is something covering up the truth of the facts. Therefore, a brilliant detective must first and foremost split open these coverings. Then, the maker of a detective film should undoubtedly gradually split open the irrelevant red herrings, and finally reveal the truth, and the audience will gradually become tense as they approach the center of the story step by step.

At the same time, the reason why detectives can solve cases is based on some clues. Therefore, the makers of detective films should have suggestive methods everywhere and express some clues. In this way, the protagonist can naturally solve the case and will not be unreasonable, and sensitive audiences will also speculate because of these clues. If things are unexpected but still reasonable, the audience will definitely be even more amazed. Therefore, the shortcomings of "Rose Villa" are things that should be paid attention to in general detective films!

Artistic Seas and Overseas Tales

Cecil B. DeMille on How to Select New Talent

— Huang Yingdai

How do we select new stars? This is indeed a question worth studying. The great director Cecil B. DeMille can select them with just one glance. He still uses this method. He uses a method of practical testing, having the actors try out, or shooting a reel of film, but in this film, he can decide whether to keep or discard them in just a moment.

His past discoveries have all been based on a glance. Before Swanson became his actor, he only saw her once on screen in a bathing comedy. He also saw a thin, dark woman leaning against the door in just a glance. "Her figure, the way she leaned against the door, I was deeply convinced that this woman had ample ability," Cecil B. DeMille said. "Before she had work, I found out her name and called her to see me." This is how Swanson's work on the screen began.

Bebe Daniels was another one, selected by Cecil B. DeMille in a glance. At that time, one day, she was shooting a two-reel comedy directed by Rockett. Cecil B. DeMille went to the studio and only watched eight feet of film. He promoted and helped her as soon as Bebe Daniels performed it. Bebe Daniels' subsequent success on the screen began at this time.

This is Cecil B. DeMille's opinion. He never likes actors to visit him. He said: "The impression of a personal visit cannot be used as a standard for selecting actors. They are completely different on and off the screen. In a film or a practical test, we can see what their personality is like and what their impression is like. I believe in the integrity of the camera as a standard for selection, and the result has never been deceived."

However, his conditions for selecting actors are an exception when it comes to Alice Terry. Years ago, she worked in Cecil B. DeMille's editing room. This editing room was very close to his office. Every time he went from his office to the editing room, he saw this young beauty working in a hurry. He never thought of putting her on the screen. Until one day, an actor walked away in the middle of filming. She only shot a small part. He had to find someone to replace her immediately, otherwise it would waste a lot of time. He sent someone to the editing room to transfer her to replace her. She performed very well in this short film. As a result, she never returned to the editing room permanently. Does it seem too imprudent for Cecil B. DeMille to choose actors in this way? But he has never been deceived.

Seeking Chinese Translation of "The Cherry Orchard"

Someone wants a copy of the Chinese translation of "The Cherry Orchard." This book was originally written by the Russian Chekhov and compiled into the Russian Drama Selection by the Commercial Press, seemingly as the ninth volume. The book is now out of print. If anyone is willing to sell or temporarily lend it, I am prepared to pay a considerable price as compensation. Please send letters through Ling Hejun of this publication.

Film Novels for National Glory (4)

— Xie Yuesheng

Boom… boom… boom… clap… clap… clap… This burst of fierce gunfire exploded the January 28th battle. Enemy soldiers poured into China like a tide. Our land, security, lives, property, wives, lovers, parents, and children were either occupied or massacred by them. A tragic battle cry awakened Tianxiong's love dream. He resolutely gathered patriotic comrades to prepare for national salvation work.

Fight for national glory! Fight for national survival! In the rumbling of gunfire, Tianxiong and Hongyu led the heroic youths toward the station. The clever Xuefang specially made a badge for "National Glory" and gave it to Tianxiong, wishing them to work hard to kill the enemy and win glory for the country.

Kill… kill… kill… Tianxiong commanded the soldiers and joined the front line to desperately kill the enemy. They fought in the trenches like this for more than half a month. The brave Tianxiong was injured for bravely killing the enemy.

Xuefang received the news of Tianxiong's injury and immediately rushed to the hospital to visit him. She carefully took care of him. In just a few days, Tianxiong's injury was completely healed. She developed love and respect out of admiration.

"We were so worried when we got the news of your injury," she said sincerely, supporting the slightly lame Tianxiong as he stumbled to a stone grain mill.

"Thank you, but it is right to die for the country," Tianxiong replied with a smile. They felt a kind of inner joy.

The citizens of the Republic of China should all be like Tianxiong. Su Rong was urging and encouraging himself. He felt that the seedlings of love between Xuefang and Tianxiong were harvested from Tianxiong's patriotic struggle. He heard Xuefang and Tianxiong's words introducing Hongyu to him, and felt ashamed as if he had been insulted. He decided to participate in the work of resisting the enemy.

The area of the war gradually expanded. The divine broadsword team bravely attacked the enemy. Su Rong commanded the soldiers, killing the enemy soldiers and begging for their lives. Our army continued to occupy the enemy's lines and finally achieved the final victory.

The ceasefire agreement put an end to the war. The news of Su Rong's death in battle spread to the rear, giving the people an encouraging spirit of patriotism and inspiring respect and admiration. This news made Hongyu and Xuefang feel sad and weep.

A round of residual sunset hung upside down in the corner of the western sky, and it had lost its inherent intensity. The evening bell of Dang… Dang… Dang was sent out from the ancient pagoda, containing a miserable and sad aftertaste.

In front of the brand-new Monument to the Loyal Souls of the Martyrs, stood a pair of young couples and a girl in plain clothes, mourning the loyal soul of this deceased martyr. From the silent tombstone, a voice vaguely came out… long-term resistance…recover lost land… (End)
